Normal: Source Material
Normal: This interpretation is based on Kumārajīva's Classical Chinese translation of the Lotus Sutra (Miào Fǎ Liánhuá Jing, 妙法蓮華經), completed in 406 CE. The original Sanskrit text is known as the Saddharma-Puṇḍarīka Sutra, a foundational Mahāyāna Buddhist scripture.
Normal: About This Interpretation
Normal: This is not a literal translation but rather a creative interpretation of Buddhist dharma presented through blues and gospel vernacular. The work honors the classical Buddhist teachings while making the spiritual wisdom accessible through contemporary African American musical and linguistic traditions. The complete text includes all twenty-eight chapters, with interpretation notes providing scholarly context and commentary on stylistic choices.
Normal: Content Information
Normal: This audiobook edition contains: Complete text of all 28 chapters • Interpretation notes for scholarly context • Professional audiobook formatting with chapter divisions and section breaks • Full preservation of Buddhist terminology and Sanskrit diacritical marks • Complete blues/gospel vernacular interpretation.
Normal: Technical Information
Normal: This document is encoded in UTF-8 format to preserve all special characters, including Sanskrit diacritics (ā, ṇ, ś, ṃ, etc.) and Buddhist terminology. All proper names and characters are spelled exactly as they appear in classical Buddhist texts.

Normal: This manuscript is formatted for professional audiobook production using ElevenReader's AI voice narration platform. The document includes proper heading hierarchy, page breaks between chapters, and semantic formatting for optimal text-to-speech processing.

Heading 2: PREFACE
Heading 3: How This Teaching Made It to Us
Normal: Told by Dao Xuan, monk of Mount Zhongnan, Tang Dynasty
Normal: Now let me tell you how this teaching got here.
Normal: This Lotus Sutra - this teaching of the Wonderful Dharma - it's the reason why the Buddhas even bother coming down here in the first place. It's the heart of the matter, the real deal, the thing they came to say. This teaching was kept safe over there in India - that great land where wisdom grows - kept there for more than a thousand years before anybody ever thought to bring it east.
Normal: Three hundred some years ago, it crossed the mountains and came to China. And I'm gonna tell you how that happened, 'cause it's a story worth knowing.
Normal: First time anybody tried to put this sutra into Chinese, it was back in the Western Jin Dynasty, during Emperor Hui's Yongkang years. There was this teacher - they called him a Bodhisattva - name of Dharmarakṣa, come from Dunhuang way out west where the desert meets the mountains. He was living by the Azure Gate in Chang'an - that's the old capital, you know - and he sat down with these ancient Sanskrit texts and did his best to turn 'em into Chinese. Called his version "The Sutra of the Correct Dharma Lotus." That was the first.
Normal: Then come the Eastern Jin Dynasty, Emperor An's Longan years, over in the Later Qin kingdom during what they called the Hongshi era. There was this monk from Kucha - that's way out there on the Silk Road - name of Kumārajīva. Now Kumārajīva, he was something special. He took that same sutra and translated it fresh, and he called it "The Lotus Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma." That's the one you got in your hands right now. That's the one we been reading all these years.
Normal: Later on, in the Sui Dynasty during the Renshou years, there was a third teacher - Jñānagupta from Northern India, living at the Great Xingshan Monastery. He made another translation, called it "The Wonderful Dharma" too.
Normal: So now we got three versions, three different ways of saying the same thing. They overlap here and there, they put things different ways, but they all trying to get at that same truth. And you know what? The one folks took to heart, the one that really caught on, was Kumārajīva's version - that Qin dynasty translation. That's the one we been studying, the one we been living with. (There's other pieces floating around too - chapters here, verses there - but we ain't talking about those today. That's for the history books.)
Normal: Now let me tell you why this teaching matters.
Normal: When the Holy Mountain showed its signs, when the sacred peaks started manifesting wonders, it took the Great Sage himself to open up that teaching, to crack it wide for people to see. And even then, even when he started teaching, it could only reach the folks who had the connection from way back - folks who'd known him before, in other lives, other times. That's just how karma works.
Normal: So first, at the Deer Park, when the Buddha started teaching, he had to divide things up. Some folks were ready for the small vehicle, some were ready for the great. Some needed the simple teachings to start with, some could handle the deep stuff right away. That's why there's different levels to this thing.
Normal: Then later, at the Golden River when he was about to leave this world, he had to make it clear again: some teachings are partial, some teachings are complete. Some give you a piece of the truth, some give you the whole picture. And here's the thing - it ain't about one assembly being better than another. The teaching meets people where they're at. It comes at the right time, in the right way, for the right folks.
Normal: You remember when five thousand people got up and walked out of the assembly? Folks think they was just arrogant, just full of themselves. But maybe they was supposed to leave. Maybe they needed to go deal with that pride before they could hear what was coming next. That's what I'm saying - everything happens for a reason.
Normal: And those five hundred who got their prophecies, who got told they gonna be Buddhas one day? They was all part of the secret teaching, the hidden work that's been going on all along.
Normal: That's why the Buddha put on that light show at the beginning - emitting that ray from between his eyebrows, lighting up all them worlds to the east. He was opening up the teaching, giving folks a reason to ask questions. He came out of that meditation and started talking about Buddha-wisdom, that big understanding that sees it all.
Normal: He told 'em about the burning house - how you gotta get out before the flames take you down, how you need that Great Vehicle to carry you to safety.
Normal: He told 'em about that phantom city - how sometimes you need a place to rest on the long journey, even if it ain't the final destination. How those old connections, those friendships from way back, they don't just disappear. They keep you moving forward.
Normal: He told 'em about the jewel sewn in the robe - how you been carrying the treasure all along, even when you was drunk and didn't know it. How your true nature been right there the whole time, just waiting for you to remember.
Normal: He told 'em about boring for water - how there's a hundred ways to get to that underground stream, how you can't give up just 'cause the dirt looks dry. You gotta keep digging, keep searching, 'cause the water's down there somewhere.
Normal: All these words, all these stories - they clear as day when you look at 'em, but they pointing to something far off, something you gotta travel toward. And if it wasn't for the Great Compassion - that Buddha's heart that can't stand to see folks drowning in their confusion, sinking in their suffering - none of this teaching would've come forth. If it wasn't for that ultimate compassionate heart, wanting to save folks who done lost their way, who done forgot who they really are - we wouldn't have none of this.
Normal: Now I'm gonna tell you something that'll make you sit up and pay attention.
Normal: From the Han Dynasty all the way through to right now, here in the Tang Dynasty, that's more than six hundred years. In all that time, they done translated over four thousand scrolls of Buddhist scriptures - four thousand! - brought 'em all the way from India, turned 'em all into Chinese. Libraries full of wisdom, stacks and stacks of teachings.
Normal: But you know which one folks hold onto most? You know which one they read and chant and study more than any other? This one. This Lotus Sutra right here.
Normal: Why you think that is?
Normal: Maybe it's 'cause this teaching speaks to something in folks, touches some old memory from way back. They say we was all there at the teaching of Buddha Wisdom Victory, eons and eons ago. Maybe this sutra waking up something that's been sleeping all this time.
Normal: Maybe everybody who hears this teaching and feels that deep respect, that reverence rising up in their heart - maybe they all got merit left over from King Awesome Sound of the World, from when he was teaching the Dharma long ago. Maybe they earning interest on an investment they don't even remember making.
Normal: That's why I wrote this preface right here at the start of the sutra. I'm hoping - and I'm praying - that we can get our six senses cleaned up, purified, so we can look up and see that wonderful gathering with the Compassionate Honored One. I'm hoping we can perfect them four virtues quick, so we can head on toward that Pure Land, that place where everything's clear and bright.
Normal: The praise for this teaching, it don't run out. It goes on and on, like a river that don't stop flowing. And I'm writing it down here so it can keep going, so it can be passed on to all the people who coming after us, all the generations yet to be born.
Normal: May they receive it. May they understand it. May they live it.
Normal: That's all I got to say.
Heading 2: INTRODUCTION
Heading 3: WHAT IS THIS TRANSLATION?
Normal: This is a blues and gospel-inflected English translation of the Lotus Sutra (Saddharma-puṇḍarīka-sūtra), one of the most revolutionary and influential Buddhist texts. Rather than offering a literal or scholarly translation, this version channels the wisdom of the Lotus Sutra through the spiritual, rhythmic, and deeply human language of African American blues and gospel tradition.

The source text is Kumārajīva's Classical Chinese version (406 CE), a translation that itself was revolutionary in making Buddhist teachings accessible to common people. This blues version continues that democratizing tradition—bringing the Dharma into living, breathing language that speaks to the soul.
Heading 3: WHY BLUES?
Normal: The blues and the Lotus Sutra share a profound spiritual sensibility:

• Both speak to suffering and its transformation.
• Both celebrate human dignity in the face of adversity.
• Both offer a way out: through music/Dharma, through community, through trust.
• Both are rooted in African American/Buddhist wisdom traditions that center on justice, compassion, and the liberation of ALL beings.

The blues doesn't shy away from pain. Neither does the Lotus Sutra. But both offer redemption, not escape. Both say: your suffering matters, your journey matters, and you are worthy of enlightenment/freedom.
Heading 3: GENDER-INCLUSIVE APPROACH
Normal: This translation is fully gender-inclusive while maintaining theological depth. The original Lotus Sutra was revolutionary for its time in affirming that women could achieve Buddhahood. This version amplifies that revolutionary message by:

• Using inclusive language ("brothers and sisters") in universal teachings.
• Maintaining male narrative where it provides contrast for women's paradigm-shifting appearances (especially the dragon princess in Chapter 12).
• Centering women bodhisattvas (Avalokiteśvara, Mahāprajāpatī, the queen) as agents of compassion and power.
• Honoring the text's original radical stance: women are not obstacles to enlightenment—they are its agents.
Heading 3: THE 28 CHAPTERS
Normal: The Lotus Sutra contains 28 chapters, each exploring a different dimension of enlightenment. Early chapters establish the Buddha's core teaching (Chapters 1-7). Middle chapters extend enlightenment to all beings (Chapters 8-11). Later chapters detail the work of Bodhisattvas in liberating all beings (Chapters 12-28).

Read sequentially, these chapters build a powerful argument: enlightenment is not reserved for monks, not limited by gender, not dependent on when you were born. It is available to all beings, everywhere, always.
Heading 3: HOW TO READ THIS VERSION
Normal: This blues translation is designed to be:

• SPOKEN ALOUD (the rhythm and vernacular shine in performance).
• STUDIED CAREFULLY (the Buddhist teachings are doctrinally accurate).
• SAVORED FOR BEAUTY (blues poetry at its finest).
• EXPERIENCED COMMUNALLY (share it, discuss it, sing it).

The verse sections use blues rhythm, call-and-response patterns, and the spiritual depth of African American preaching traditions. The prose sections use accessible vernacular English while maintaining the elevated and reverent tone appropriate to sacred scripture.
Heading 3: ABOUT THE SOURCE TEXT
Normal: Kumārajīva (343-413 CE) was a Buddhist missionary who translated over 100 Buddhist texts into Classical Chinese. His version of the Lotus Sutra became the standard text throughout East Asia. He was known for making texts accessible without sacrificing accuracy—the same goal of this blues version.

The text's 28 chapters were compiled from earlier Sanskrit versions and represent centuries of Buddhist reflection on enlightenment, compassion, and the radical possibility of universal salvation.
Heading 3: KEY FIGURES IN THIS TEXT
Normal: • ŚĀKYAMUNI BUDDHA: The historical Buddha who teaches throughout.
• ŚĀRIPUTRA: Chief disciple, represents intellectual understanding.
• MAÑJUŚRĪ: Bodhisattva of Wisdom.
• AVALOKITEŚVARA: Bodhisattva of Compassion (appears in many forms).
• THE DRAGON PRINCESS: A revolutionary figure whose Buddhahood shatters expectations about gender and enlightenment.
• THE SIXTEEN PRINCES: Future Buddhas who point toward universal salvation.
Heading 3: ESSENTIAL BUDDHIST TERMS USED
Normal: Bodhisattva (BO-dee-SAT-vuh): A being dedicated to liberating all others.

Buddha-nature: The capacity for Buddhahood present in all beings.

Dharma: The teaching; the way things are; the law of cause and effect.

Tathāgata (tah-TAH-guh-tuh): "One who has thus gone"; epithet for the Buddha.

Samādhi: Deep meditative concentration; unified awareness.

Nirvāṇa: The cessation of suffering; enlightenment; peace beyond all concepts.
Heading 3: READING GUIDE
Normal: Each chapter includes:

• CHAPTER HEADING with number and title.
• PROSE SECTIONS: Buddhist teachings in accessible blues-inflected vernacular.
• VERSE SECTIONS: The same teachings in blues poetry and song form.
• TRANSLATION NOTES: Context and deeper meaning.

The repetition of teachings (prose then verse) is intentional. This is how the Sutra was transmitted orally for centuries—each repetition deepens the understanding. Don't skip the verses as "just repetition." They are transformation.
Heading 3: PRONUNCIATION GUIDE FOR SANSKRIT NAMES
Normal: Śākyamuni = SHAHK-yuh-MOO-nee.
Śāriputra = shah-REE-POO-truh.
Mañjuśrī = muhn-JOO-shree.
Avalokiteśvara = uh-vuh-LOW-kee-TESH-vur-uh.
Mahākāśyapa = muh-HAH-KAH-shuh-puh.
Ānanda = AH-nahn-duh.
Maitreya = my-TRAY-uh.
Mahāprajāpatī = muh-HAH-pruh-JAH-puh-tee.
Heading 3: FINAL NOTE
Normal: The Lotus Sutra ends with a profound image: the Bodhisattva of Universal Worthy rides a white elephant in all directions, bringing the Dharma to all beings. May this blues translation carry the Dharma to hearts ready to hear it. May it liberate all beings, without exception.

Om mani padme hum.
(The jewel in the heart of the lotus.)
Heading 1: CHAPTER ONE: THE OPENING
Normal: A Blues Interpretation from the Classical Chinese
Heading 2: THE GATHERING
Normal: Listen now, this is what I heard with my own ears.
Normal: One time—and ain't it always one time when truth comes calling—the Buddha was staying up on Vulture Peak Mountain, right outside the city called King's House (Rajagriha). And he wasn't alone, no sir. He had twelve thousand monks with him, every last one of them a brother who'd made it through to the other side.
Normal: These weren't no beginners, you understand. These were folks who'd walked the long hard road and come out clean. They'd dried up all the leaking wounds of craving. They'd burned out every last bit of that fever we call desire. They'd gotten what they came for, broke every chain that binds a person to this wheel of suffering, and their minds were finally free—free like a bird that's been caged all its life and somebody finally opens the door.
Normal: Let me tell you their names, 'cause names matter when you talking about the ones who made it through:
Normal: There was Ājñāta-Kauṇḍinya, the first one to understand what the Buddha was laying down. There was Mahākāśyapa, that stern old man who knew how to live with nothing. There was Uruvilvā-Kāśyapa and his brothers Gayā-Kāśyapa and Nadī-Kāśyapa—three brothers who all found the way. There was Śāriputra, sharp as a razor, and Mahā-Maudgalyāyana, who could work wonders. There was Mahā-Kātyāyana, who could preach, and Aniruddha, who could see what others couldn't. There was Kapphina and Gavāmpati and Revata and Pilindavatsa and Bakkula and Mahā-Kauṣṭhila and Nanda and Sundarananda and Pūrṇa-Maitrāyaṇīputra, the one who could really teach, and Subhūti, who understood emptiness like breathing, and Ānanda, who remembered everything the Buddha ever said, and Rāhula, the Buddha's own son.
Normal: These were the famous ones, the ones everybody knew about, the ones who'd gone all the way.
Normal: And there were two thousand more—some still learning, some already done with learning—all walking that path.
Normal: And Mahāprajāpatī Gautamī, the nun who raised the Buddha when his mama died, she was there with six thousand sisters following her. And Yaśodharā, the one who used to be the Buddha's wife before he left to find the truth, she was there too with her own followers.
Normal: But that ain't all. No sir, that ain't even half of it.
Normal: There were eighty thousand bodhisattvas—and when I say bodhisattva, I'm talking about the ones who've set their hearts on the highest freedom, not just for themselves but for everybody. They weren't gonna turn back, no matter what. They'd gotten hold of something called dhāraṇī—that's like a power to hold onto the truth no matter how hard the wind blows. They could speak smooth and clear about the deepest things, and they kept the wheel of teaching rolling forward, never backing up.
Normal: They'd served countless Buddhas—I'm talking about hundreds, thousands, millions of enlightened teachers. They'd planted good seeds in all those Buddha-fields, and every Buddha they ever met spoke their names with respect. They'd trained their hearts in loving-kindness until kindness was just who they were. They'd gotten inside the Buddha's wisdom like you get inside your own house. They'd crossed over to the far shore of understanding, and their names rang out through countless worlds. They could guide countless beings through the darkness.
Normal: Let me tell you some of their names:
Normal: There was Mañjuśrī, who carries the sword of wisdom. There was Avalokiteśvara, who hears every cry of suffering in this world. There was Mahāsthāmaprāpta, the one with great power. There was Always Striving, who never lets up. There was Never Resting, who don't know how to quit. There was Jewel Palm and Medicine King and Brave Giving and Jewel Moon and Moon Light and Full Moon. There was Great Strength and Limitless Strength and Beyond the Triple World. There was Bhadrapāla and Maitreya—that's the one who's gonna be the next Buddha when this age runs out. There was Jewel Accumulation and Guide—eighty thousand of these great-hearted teachers, all gathered there.
Normal: And the heavenly beings showed up too, you better believe it.
Normal: Śakra, the king of the thirty-three heavens, he came down with twenty thousand divine children. And there was Moon Prince and Universal Fragrance and Jewel Light and the Four Great Kings, each one bringing ten thousand children of heaven. And Freedom King and Great Freedom King, they brought thirty thousand. And Brahmā Sahāmpati, the lord of this whole world-system, and Śikhin Brahma and Bright Brahma, they came with twelve thousand divine children.
Normal: And eight dragon kings came swimming up from the deep waters: Nanda and Upananda and Sāgara and Vāsukin and Takṣaka and Anavatapta and Manasvin and Utpalaka—each one with hundreds of thousands following behind.
Normal: And four kings of the kinnaras came—those are the singers, the ones who make music for the gods. There was Dharma Kinnara King and Wonderful Dharma Kinnara King and Great Dharma Kinnara King and Dharma-Holding Kinnara King, all with their companies.
Normal: And four kings of the gandharvas—those are the heavenly musicians. There was Joy and Joyful Sound and Beautiful and Beautiful Sound, all with their followers.
Normal: And four kings of the asuras came too—those are the jealous spirits, always fighting with the gods: Bālin and Kharaskandha and Vemacitrin and Rāhu, each one leading hundreds of thousands.
Normal: And four kings of the garuḍas—those giant birds—came flying down: Great Virtue and Great Body and Great Fullness and As-You-Wish, each one with their flocks.
Normal: And King Ajātaśatru, son of Queen Vaidehi, he came with hundreds of thousands of people from the city.
Normal: Every single one of them bowed down at the Buddha's feet—and when I say feet, I mean they got low, they showed respect—and then they sat down off to the side.
Heading 2: THE TEACHING BEFORE THE SILENCE
Normal: Right then, the Buddha was surrounded on all four sides—monks, nuns, laymen, laywomen—all of them offering him respect, honoring him, praising him. And he started teaching them a scripture of the Great Vehicle, a text called "The Sutra of Immeasurable Meanings"—a teaching for those bodhisattvas, a teaching that the Buddha himself protects and keeps in mind.
Normal: When he finished teaching that sutra, he crossed his legs up under him—you know that sitting position, like a locked-up lotus—and he entered into a deep, deep meditation on infinite meanings. His body went still. His mind went still. He wasn't moving at all.
Normal: And right then, heaven started raining flowers—mandarava flowers and great mandarava flowers, manjusaka flowers and great manjusaka flowers—pouring down on the Buddha and all that great assembly. And the whole Buddha-world shook six different ways—you know that shaking when the earth can't hold still 'cause something holy is happening.
Normal: And everybody in that gathering—the monks and nuns, the laymen and laywomen, the dragons and the night-wandering spirits, the gandharvas and asuras and garudas and kinnaras and mahoragas, the humans and non-humans, all the little kings and the wheel-turning holy kings—every last one of them got something they never had before. Joy rose up in them. They put their palms together and they looked at the Buddha with one mind, all together, not turning away.
Heading 2: THE LIGHT FROM BETWEEN THE EYEBROWS
Normal: And then the Buddha sent out a beam of light from between his eyebrows—right from that white hair-mark there—and it lit up eighteen thousand worlds to the east, every last corner of them, down to the deepest hell called Avīci where suffering don't quit, all the way up to Akaniṣṭha Heaven where the highest gods dwell.
Normal: And from this world here, you could see into all those other lands. You could see beings in all six paths of existence—beings in hell, hungry ghosts, animals, humans, jealous spirits, gods—you could see them all. And you could see the Buddhas in those worlds, teaching right now, hear the words they were saying. And you could see monks and nuns and laymen and laywomen, people walking the path and getting somewhere. You could see bodhisattvas with all kinds of causes and conditions, all kinds of faith and understanding, all kinds of appearances, walking the bodhisattva road. You could see Buddhas entering that final peace beyond peace, that nirvāṇa. And you could see, after those Buddhas passed on, stupas made of seven kinds of jewels, rising up to hold their relics.
Heading 2: MAITREYA ASKS, MAÑJUŚRĪ REMEMBERS
Normal: Right then, Maitreya Bodhisattva—the one who's coming next—he thought to himself: "Now what's going on here? The World-Honored One is showing us signs and wonders. What's the cause of all this? The Buddha's gone into a meditation so deep you can't think your way into it, and he's showing us things we never seen before. Who should I ask about this? Who could answer?"
Normal: And then he thought: "This Mañjuśrī, he's the Dharma-prince, the king's son. He's served countless Buddhas in the past, no telling how many. He must've seen signs like this before. I'm gonna ask him."
Normal: And right then all the monks and nuns and layfolk and all the gods and dragons and spirits, they all thought the same thing: "This light the Buddha's shining, this supernatural sign—who can we ask about it?"
Normal: So Maitreya Bodhisattva, wanting to clear up his own doubt and seeing what everybody else was wondering, he turned to Mañjuśrī and said: "What's the cause and condition for all this? Why's he sending out this great light, lighting up eighteen thousand lands to the east, showing us all those Buddha-lands decorated so fine?"
Normal: And then Maitreya, wanting to say it again in another way, he spoke in verse. And let me tell you, these verses had rhythm:
Normal: Mañjuśrī, tell me why—
Normal: Why the Teacher's shining bright
Normal: From that white hair between his eyes,
Normal: Pouring out that great big light?
Normal: Mandarava flowers raining down,
Normal: Manjusaka falling all around,
Normal: Sandalwood wind blowing sweet,
Normal: Making everybody's heart feel sound.
Normal: That's why the ground's all pure and clean,
Normal: This whole world shaking six ways round,
Normal: The four assemblies filled with joy,
Normal: Body and mind feeling glory-bound.
Normal: Light from between his eyebrows bright,
Normal: Shining east across the land,
Normal: Eighteen thousand worlds lit up,
Normal: Every one of them turning gold like sand.
Normal: From Avīci Hell below
Normal: All the way to highest height,
Normal: In all those worlds we're seeing now
Normal: Beings walking in six paths of life.
Normal: We see where birth and death will lead them,
Normal: See the good and bad they've sown,
Normal: See the pretty and the ugly fruit they're getting—
Normal: Everything's being shown.
Normal: And we see the Buddhas too,
Normal: Those holy lion-teachers standing tall,
Normal: Teaching scriptures wonderful and subtle—
Normal: The finest teachings of them all.
Normal: Their voices pure and clear,
Normal: Speaking soft words, smooth and true,
Normal: Teaching countless bodhisattvas—
Normal: Millions, billions, more than you can count, it's true.
Normal: That Brahma-voice so deep and wonderful,
Normal: Making people want to hear,
Normal: Each one in their own world
Normal: Teaching Dharma true and clear.
Normal: Using all kinds of causes and conditions,
Normal: Countless metaphors and signs,
Normal: Lighting up the Buddha-Dharma,
Normal: Opening up people's minds.
Normal: If someone's suffering hard,
Normal: Sick and tired of getting old and dying sick,
Normal: They'll teach nirvāṇa to them—
Normal: That'll end suffering quick.
Normal: If someone's got good fortune,
Normal: Served Buddhas way back when,
Normal: Looking for the highest teaching,
Normal: They'll teach the solitary path to them.
Normal: If there's Buddha's children there
Normal: Walking many different roads,
Normal: Seeking wisdom highest of all,
Normal: They'll teach the pure path to unfold.
Normal: Mañjuśrī, sitting here,
Normal: I'm seeing and I'm hearing all of this,
Normal: A thousand billion different things—
Normal: More than I can tell you, more than I can list.
Normal: I'm seeing countless bodhisattvas,
Normal: Sands-of-the-Ganges many, seeking Buddha's way,
Normal: Some of them practicing giving—
Normal: Gold and silver, coral fine,
Normal: Pearls and magic jewels,
Normal: Conch shells, agate, diamonds that shine,
Normal: Servants, carriages, everything they own,
Normal: Precious decorated sedan chairs—
Normal: Giving it all with happy hearts,
Normal: Dedicating it to Buddha's care,
Normal: Hoping for that supreme vehicle,
Normal: The one all Buddhas praise everywhere.
Normal: Some bodhisattvas giving four-horse jeweled carts,
Normal: Railings and flower canopies decorated so nice.
Normal: And I see bodhisattvas giving their own flesh and limbs,
Normal: Even wives and children—that's the ultimate sacrifice,
Normal: Seeking that road to wisdom supreme.
Normal: I see bodhisattvas giving heads and eyes and bodies,
Normal: Happy to offer them all up,
Normal: Seeking Buddha-wisdom—
Normal: Filling that wisdom-cup.
Normal: Mañjuśrī, I see kings
Normal: Going to where Buddha stays,
Normal: Asking about the highest path,
Normal: Then giving up their pleasant kingdoms, palaces and all,
Normal: Shaving off their hair,
Normal: Putting on the Dharma robes—
Normal: Answering that highest call.
Normal: I see bodhisattvas becoming monks,
Normal: Living alone in quiet places,
Normal: Happy to chant the scriptures day and night,
Normal: Peace all over their faces.
Normal: I see bodhisattvas brave and vigorous,
Normal: Going into deep mountains where the world can't follow,
Normal: Thinking about the Buddha's path,
Normal: Where the truth ain't hollow.
Normal: I see ones who've left desire behind,
Normal: Always staying in empty space,
Normal: Going deep into meditation,
Normal: Getting five spiritual powers by grace.
Normal: I see bodhisattvas sitting quiet in meditation, palms together,
Normal: Praising the Dharma-kings
Normal: With thousands and millions of verses—
Normal: Singing those wisdom-things.
Normal: I see bodhisattvas with wisdom deep and will firm,
Normal: Able to question all the Buddhas,
Normal: Hearing everything and holding onto it—
Normal: Not letting go of nothing, never.
Normal: I see Buddha-children
Normal: With meditation and wisdom both complete,
Normal: Using countless metaphors
Normal: To teach the assembly, making wisdom sweet,
Normal: Happy to be teaching Dharma,
Normal: Transforming bodhisattvas all around,
Normal: Breaking the demon armies,
Normal: Beating that Dharma drum sound!
Normal: I see bodhisattvas silent and peaceful,
Normal: Gods and dragons respecting them all the way—
Normal: But they don't get happy about it,
Normal: Don't let it make their day.
Normal: I see bodhisattvas in forests sending out light,
Normal: Relieving the suffering of hell,

Heading 2: MAÑJUŚRĪ REMEMBERS THE ANCIENT PATTERN
Normal: Right then, Mañjuśrī spoke to Maitreya Bodhisattva and all those great beings and good men, saying:
Normal: "The way I figure it, the World-Honored One right now is about to teach a great Dharma, about to rain down a great Dharma-rain, about to blow the great Dharma-conch, about to beat the great Dharma-drum, about to explain the great Dharma-meaning.
Normal: "Good men, in the past, with other Buddhas, I've seen signs like this. After they let out this kind of light, they taught the great Dharma. So you should know: the Buddha's showing this light now for the same reason. He wants to help all living beings hear and know this Dharma that's hard for the whole world to believe. That's why he's showing these signs."
Normal: And Mañjuśrī started telling a story—a story from so long ago you can't count the years:
Normal: "Good men, way back in the past—I'm talking about countless, boundless, inconceivable, uncountable eons ago—there was a Buddha called Moon-Sun-Lamp Thus Come One, Worthy of Offerings, Perfectly Enlightened, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Unsurpassed One, Tamer of Beings, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One.
Normal: "He taught the true Dharma—good in the beginning, good in the middle, good in the end. His meaning was deep and far-reaching. His words were skillful and wonderful. Pure and unmixed, complete and perfect, he laid out what the holy life looks like.
Normal: "For people seeking to be hearers, he taught the Dharma of the Four Noble Truths—how to cross over birth and old age and sickness and death, how to reach the final peace of nirvāṇa.
Normal: "For people seeking to be solitary realizers, he taught the Dharma of the Twelve Links of Dependent Origination.
Normal: "For the bodhisattvas, he taught the Six Perfections—how to attain that highest perfect awakening, how to accomplish all-knowing wisdom."
Normal: And then Mañjuśrī said something that'll make you sit up:
Normal: "And then there was another Buddha, also called Moon-Sun-Lamp. And then another Buddha, also called Moon-Sun-Lamp. Like this, twenty thousand Buddhas, all with the same name—Moon-Sun-Lamp. And they all had the same family name too: Bharadvāja.
Normal: "Maitreya, you should know: from the first Buddha to the last Buddha, they all had the same name, Moon-Sun-Lamp, complete with all ten titles. And the Dharma they taught was good in the beginning, middle, and end.
Normal: "Now that last Moon-Sun-Lamp Buddha, before he left home to seek the way, he had eight sons. Their names were: Having Intent, Good Intent, Infinite Intent, Jewel Intent, Increasing Intent, Doubt-Removing Intent, Toward Intent, and Dharma Intent.
Normal: "These eight princes had power and dignity and freedom. Each one ruled over four continents. When these princes heard that their father had left home and attained the highest perfect awakening, every one of them gave up their kingdoms and followed him into homelessness. They raised their minds to the Great Vehicle, always practiced the holy life, and all became Dharma-teachers. They'd already planted roots of goodness with thousands and millions of Buddhas.
Normal: "Now when that Moon-Sun-Lamp Buddha taught the scripture of the Great Vehicle called 'Sutra of Infinite Meanings'—a teaching for bodhisattvas, a teaching that Buddha protects and keeps in mind—after he finished teaching it, right there in the great assembly, he crossed his legs up into meditation and entered that concentration on infinite meanings. His body and mind stopped moving.
Normal: "And right then, heaven rained down mandarava flowers, great mandarava flowers, manjusaka flowers, great manjusaka flowers, scattering them on the Buddha and the great assembly. And the whole Buddha-world shook six ways.
Normal: "And then everybody in the assembly—monks, nuns, laymen, laywomen, gods, dragons, night-wanderers, gandharvas, asuras, garudas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans and non-humans, all the little kings and wheel-turning holy kings—all of them got something they never had before. Joy! They put their palms together and looked at the Buddha with one mind."
Normal: Mañjuśrī kept going with his story:
Normal: "And then that Thus Come One let out a beam of light from between his eyebrows, lighting up eighteen thousand Buddha-lands to the east, reaching everywhere, just like the lands we're seeing right now.
Normal: "Maitreya, you should know: in that assembly back then, there were two billion bodhisattvas who wanted to hear the Dharma. When these bodhisattvas saw that light shining all over those Buddha-lands, they got something they never had before, and they wanted to know what that light was about.
Normal: "There was a bodhisattva there named Wonderful Light, and he had eight hundred disciples.
Normal: "Right then, Moon-Sun-Lamp Buddha came out of his meditation and, turning to Wonderful Light Bodhisattva, he taught the scripture of the Great Vehicle called 'The Lotus Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma'—a teaching for bodhisattvas, a teaching that Buddha protects and keeps in mind.
Normal: "He taught that sutra for sixty short eons, never getting up from his seat. And everybody listening sat there in one place for sixty short eons, their bodies and minds not moving, hearing what the Buddha said, and it felt like just the time it takes to eat a meal. During all that time, there wasn't a single person whose body or mind got tired or restless.
Normal: "After Moon-Sun-Lamp Buddha finished teaching that sutra for sixty short eons, he made this announcement to the assembly of Brahmas and Maras and ascetics and brahmins and gods and humans and asuras:
Normal: "'Tonight at midnight, the Thus Come One will enter the nirvāṇa without remainder.'
Normal: "There was a bodhisattva there named Virtue Storehouse. Moon-Sun-Lamp Buddha gave him a prediction right then and there. He told all the monks: 'This Virtue Storehouse Bodhisattva will be the next Buddha. His name will be Pure Body, Tathāgata, Arhat, Perfectly Enlightened.'
Normal: "After giving this prediction, at midnight, Buddha entered the nirvāṇa without remainder.
Normal: "After the Buddha passed on, Wonderful Light Bodhisattva held onto that Lotus Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma and taught it to people for eighty short eons.
Normal: "Now those eight sons of Moon-Sun-Lamp Buddha all became students of Wonderful Light. Wonderful Light taught and transformed them, made them firm in their resolve for the highest perfect awakening. After they'd made offerings to countless hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of Buddhas, they all attained Buddhahood. The last one to become a Buddha was named Burning Lamp.
Normal: "Among those eight hundred disciples, there was one person called Seeker of Fame. He was greedy for gain and offerings. Even though he'd study and recite all kinds of scriptures, he didn't really get them—he'd forget most of what he learned. That's why they called him Seeker of Fame.
Normal: "But even he, through planting various roots of goodness, got to meet countless hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of Buddhas, make offerings to them, honor them, respect them, praise them."
Normal: And then Mañjuśrī brought it all home:
Normal: "Maitreya, you should know: that Wonderful Light Bodhisattva back then—you think he was somebody else? He was me. I'm that person.
Normal: "And that Seeker of Fame Bodhisattva? That was you. You're that person.
Normal: "Now I'm seeing these signs, and they're no different from what I saw before. That's why I figure: today the Thus Come One is about to teach that scripture of the Great Vehicle called 'The Lotus Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma,' a teaching for bodhisattvas, a teaching that Buddha protects and keeps in mind."

Heading 2: INTERPRETATION NOTES:
Normal: This interpretation takes Kumārajīva's Classical Chinese text and pours it through the blues tradition—that great river of African American spiritual and musical expression that's always known how to carry deep wisdom in everyday language.
Normal: What I kept:
Normal: - The famous names like Mañjuśrī, Avalokiteśvara, Śāriputra, Maitreya
Normal: - The sequence and structure of the original
Normal: - The depth of meaning—blues ain't shallow, and neither is this sutra
Normal: What I changed:
Normal: - Technical terms became lived experience: "阿羅漢" became people who "made it through to the other side," who "dried up all the leaking wounds of craving"
Normal: - Descriptive names got translated: "日月燈明如來" became "Moon-Sun-Lamp Thus Come One"
Normal: - The eight princes: 有意 became "Having Intent," 善意 became "Good Intent," and so on
Normal: - Abstract Buddhist terms became concrete images: nirvāṇa is "that final peace beyond peace," meditation is going so deep "you can't think your way into it," dhāraṇī is "a power to hold onto the truth no matter how hard the wind blows"
Normal: The verses especially got the blues treatment—repetition, rhythm, call-and-response feeling, direct address ("Listen now," "you hear me?"), the music of the language itself.
Normal: This Chapter One tells the story of the great gathering on Vulture Peak, the Buddha's mysterious entry into meditation, the light from between his eyebrows showing countless worlds, Maitreya's question, and Mañjuśrī's memory of ancient Buddhas doing the same thing before teaching the Lotus Sutra. It's the opening act, the gathering storm before the great teaching comes.
Normal: The blues has always carried sacred truth in the language of the people. This interpretation tries to honor both traditions—the ancient Buddhist teaching and the deep American wisdom-stream that knows how to make the high come low, the distant come near, and the abstract become as real as your own heartbeat.
Heading 1: CHAPTER TWO: THE LOVING TRICKS
Normal: A Blues Interpretation from the Classical Chinese
Heading 2: THE BUDDHA SPEAKS OF DEEP WISDOM
Normal: Now at that time, you see, the World-Honored One—he rose up from his meditation, rose up calm and peaceful-like, and he turned to Śāriputra and said:
Normal: "Listen here, Śāriputra. The wisdom of the Buddhas—it goes down deep, deeper than any well you ever tried to draw from. It's measureless, you hear me? Can't nobody measure how deep it goes. The door to that wisdom, now—it's hard to understand, hard to get through. All them disciples and solitary-walkers, all them learned folks who think they got it figured—they can't know this thing.
Normal: "And why's that? I'm gonna tell you why. The Buddha, he walked alongside a hundred thousand million billion Buddhas, ain't no way to count them all. He practiced every single path those Buddhas taught, every last one. Brave and fierce, he walked them roads. His name got known everywhere, you understand? He accomplished things so deep, things never done before. And when he teaches, he speaks according to what folks need, but what he's really getting at—that's hard to understand.
Normal: "Śāriputra, ever since I became a Buddha, I been using all kinds of causes, all kinds of stories, all kinds of comparisons, pouring out teachings like water. Countless loving tricks, that's what I been using, leading people, guiding them away from all their clinging and holding on. And why can I do this? Because the Tathāgata, he's perfected all them skillful means, all that perfect knowing and seeing.
Normal: "Śāriputra, the Tathāgata's knowing and seeing—it's vast and deep and far-reaching. It's without measure, without any walls or boundaries. He got the powers, he got the fearlessness, he got the meditations and the liberations and the deep states—he's gone into them without any bottom to hit. He's accomplished everything that ain't never been accomplished before.
Normal: "Śāriputra, the Tathāgata, he can break things down every which way, explain the teachings with skill, and his words—they soft, they gentle, they please every heart.
Normal: "Śāriputra, let me put it to you straight: all them measureless, boundless, never-been-done things—the Buddha's accomplished them all."
Normal: Then the Buddha said: "Stop, Śāriputra. Don't need to say no more. And why's that? What the Buddha's accomplished—it's the rarest, hardest-to-understand thing there is. Only a Buddha together with a Buddha can exhaust the true reality of all things. That means: the suchness of their appearance, the suchness of their nature, the suchness of their substance, the suchness of their power, the suchness of their function, the suchness of their causes, the suchness of their conditions, the suchness of their effects, the suchness of their results, and the suchness of their beginning and end being ultimately equal."
Normal: The Hero of the World—can't measure him,
Normal: All them heavenly beings and worldly folk,
Normal: Every kind of living creature there is—
Normal: Ain't nobody can know the Buddha's truth.
Normal: The Buddha's powers and his fearlessness,
Normal: His liberations and his deep meditations,
Normal: And all them other Buddha-things he got—
Normal: Ain't nobody can measure what he knows.
Normal: From countless Buddhas he learned his way,
Normal: Walked every single road there was to walk,
Normal: The dharma deep and subtle, hard to see,
Normal: So difficult to understand and know.
Normal: For measureless millions upon millions of ages,
Normal: He walked all them roads till he walked them through,
Normal: Reached the place of awakening, got the fruit—
Normal: I done seen it all, I know it all.
Normal: A fruit as great as this one here,
Normal: All its different natures, meanings, marks—
Normal: Only me and all them Buddhas in ten directions,
Normal: Only we can know this thing.
Normal: This dharma—can't be shown by pointing,
Normal: Words fall silent when you try to speak it,
Normal: All them other kinds of living beings—
Normal: Ain't nobody among them understands,
Normal: Except for the bodhisattvas,
Normal: Them whose faith-power stands strong and firm.

Normal: Still couldn't know the Buddha's wisdom.

Heading 2: THE ASSEMBLY'S DOUBT AND ŚĀRIPUTRA'S REQUEST
Normal: At that time, in the great assembly, there was disciples—them with no more outflows, them arhats—Ājñāta-Kauṇḍinya and the rest, twelve hundred of them. And there was others too, monks and nuns, laymen and laywomen, who done set their mind on the disciple vehicle or the solitary-walker vehicle. Every one of them thought to themselves:
Normal: "Right now, why's the World-Honored One going on so earnestly, praising and exalting skillful means like this? He says the dharma the Buddha obtained is so deep and hard to understand. What he speaks about got a meaning that's difficult to know. All them disciples and solitary-walkers can't reach it. The Buddha explained one liberation doctrine—we obtained that dharma too, reached nirvāṇa with it. But now we don't know where this teaching is heading."
Normal: At that time, Śāriputra, he knew the four groups in the assembly was doubting, and he himself didn't understand it neither. So he addressed the Buddha, saying:
Normal: "World-Honored One, for what cause, for what reason are you so earnestly praising the Buddhas' foremost skillful means, this deep, subtle, difficult-to-understand dharma? From way back till now, I ain't never heard you speak like this before. Right now, all four groups got doubts. I only wish the World-Honored One would explain this matter. World-Honored One, why are you so earnestly praising this deep, subtle, difficult-to-understand dharma?"
Normal: Then Śāriputra, wanting to speak this meaning again, he said it in verse:
Normal: Sun of Wisdom, Great Holy Honored One,
Normal: After such a long time you speaking this dharma now.
Normal: You say you obtained these kind of things—
Normal: Powers, fearlessness, meditations,
Normal: Concentration, liberation, all the rest,
Normal: Inconceivable dharmas like these.
Normal: The dharma you got at the place of awakening—
Normal: Ain't nobody can raise a question about it.
Normal: My mind's so hard to fathom out,
Normal: And ain't nobody can ask about it neither.
Normal: Without nobody asking, you just speak on your own,
Normal: Praising the road you walked yourself.
Normal: Your wisdom so subtle and wonderful,
Normal: The very thing all Buddhas obtained.
Normal: Them arhats without outflow,
Normal: And them seeking nirvāṇa too—
Normal: Now they all done fell into a net of doubt,
Normal: Wondering why the Buddha speaking this.
Normal: Them seeking to be solitary-walkers,
Normal: Monks and nuns alike,
Normal: Heavenly beings, dragons, spirits, gods,
Normal: And gandharvas and such—
Normal: They looking at each other, full of wondering,
Normal: Gazing up at the Honored One of Two Feet.
Normal: What is this matter all about?
Normal: We hoping the Buddha will explain it clear.
Normal: Among all them disciple folks,
Normal: The Buddha says I'm number one.
Normal: But right now, concerning my own wisdom,
Normal: I'm doubting, confused, can't understand—
Normal: Is this the ultimate dharma here,
Normal: Or is it just the road we walk?
Normal: We who was born from the Buddha's mouth,
Normal: We standing with palms pressed together, gazing up and waiting,
Normal: Hoping you'll send forth your subtle, wonderful voice,
Normal: Speak to us at this time just like it really is.
Normal: Them heavenly beings, dragons, spirits, and gods,
Normal: Numerous as Ganges River sands,
Normal: Them bodhisattvas seeking to be Buddhas,
Normal: Eighty thousand in their great number,
Normal: And from millions and billions of lands,
Normal: Wheel-turning holy kings done arrived,
Normal: Palms pressed together with reverent minds—
Normal: They wanting to hear about the complete road.
Heading 2: THE BUDDHA'S THREE REFUSALS
Normal: At that time, the Buddha told Śāriputra: "Stop, stop. Don't need to say no more. If I speak about this matter, all them beings in all the worlds—the heavenly folk and the human folk—they all gonna be shocked and full of doubt."
Normal: Śāriputra addressed the Buddha again, saying: "World-Honored One, I only wish you would speak about it, only wish you would speak! And why's that? In this assembly here, there's countless hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of innumerable living beings who done seen Buddhas before. Their faculties are sharp and fierce, their wisdom bright and clear. When they hear what the Buddha speaks, they gonna be able to respect it and believe it."
Normal: At that time, Śāriputra, wanting to speak this meaning again, he said it in verse:
Normal: Dharma King, Most High Honored One,
Normal: Just speak it out, don't you worry none.
Normal: In this assembly of measureless folks,
Normal: There's some who can respect and believe.
Normal: The Buddha again stopped Śāriputra: "If I speak about this matter, all them beings in all the worlds—heavenly folk, human folk, asuras—they all gonna be shocked and full of doubt. And them arrogant monks, they gonna fall into the great pit."
Normal: At that time, the World-Honored One spoke again in verse, saying:
Normal: Stop, stop, don't need to speak about it.
Normal: My dharma is wonderful and hard to conceive.
Normal: Them arrogant ones full of themselves—
Normal: If they hear it, they surely won't respect or believe.
Normal: At that time, Śāriputra addressed the Buddha again: "World-Honored One, I only wish you would speak about it, only wish you would speak! Right now in this assembly here, folks like me and more—hundreds of thousands of millions of billions—world after world we been receiving the Buddha's transforming teaching. Folks like this, they surely can respect and believe. They gonna have long-night peace and safety, gonna gain much benefit."
Normal: At that time, Śāriputra, wanting to speak this meaning again, he said it in verse:
Normal: Most High Honored One of Two Feet,
Normal: I wish you'd speak the foremost dharma.
Normal: I'm the Buddha's eldest son—
Normal: I only beg you to explain it clear and distinct.
Normal: This assembly of measureless folks,
Normal: They able to respect and believe this dharma.
Normal: The Buddha already, world after world,
Normal: Done taught and transformed folks like these.
Normal: They all with one mind, palms pressed together,
Normal: Wanting to listen and receive the Buddha's words.
Normal: We twelve hundred here,
Normal: And others seeking to be Buddhas—
Normal: We wish, for the sake of this whole assembly,
Normal: You'd just explain it clear and distinct.
Normal: When these folks hear this dharma,
Normal: They gonna be born with great rejoicing.
Normal: FIVE THOUSAND LEAVE THE ASSEMBLY
Normal: At that time, the World-Honored One told Śāriputra: "You done earnestly asked three times now. How can I not speak? Now you listen carefully, think about it well, remember it good. I'm gonna break it down for you clear and distinct."
Normal: When he spoke these words, right there in the assembly there was monks and nuns, laymen and laywomen—five thousand of them—they got up from their seats, bowed to the Buddha, and walked on out. And why was that? This bunch here, their roots of wrongdoing was deep and heavy, and they was full of arrogance. They thought they'd obtained what they hadn't obtained, thought they'd realized what they hadn't realized. They had faults like these, and that's why they didn't stay. The World-Honored One just stayed silent, didn't try to stop them none.
Normal: At that time, the Buddha told Śāriputra: "Now this assembly of mine, it ain't got no more dead branches and dead leaves. It's got only the genuine, truthful, real ones. Śāriputra, them arrogant folks leaving—that's a good thing. Now you listen well. I'm gonna speak it for you."
Normal: Śāriputra said: "Yes, indeed, World-Honored One. I'm joyful, wanting to hear."
Heading 2: THE ONE GREAT MATTER—THE ONE VEHICLE
Normal: The Buddha told Śāriputra:
Normal: "A wonderful dharma like this—the Buddhas, the Tathāgatas, they only speak it from time to time. Just like the udumbara flower—it only appears once in a great while. Śāriputra, you and the rest ought to believe what the Buddha speaks. His words ain't false or empty.
Normal: "Śāriputra, when the Buddhas speak the dharma according to what's fitting, the meaning's hard to understand. And why's that? I use countless skillful means—all kinds of causes, all kinds of comparisons, all kinds of expressions—to explain the dharmas. This dharma here, it ain't something thinking and discriminating can understand. Only the Buddhas can know it.
Normal: "And why's that? The Buddhas, the World-Honored Ones, they only appear in the world for one great matter, one great cause and condition. Śāriputra, what do I mean when I say the Buddhas, the World-Honored Ones, only appear in the world for one great matter, one great cause and condition?
Normal: "The Buddhas, the World-Honored Ones, appear in the world because they want to open up the Buddha's knowing and seeing for living beings, make it pure—that's why they appear. They want to show living beings the Buddha's knowing and seeing—that's why they appear. They want to awaken living beings to the Buddha's knowing and seeing—that's why they appear. They want to cause living beings to enter into the path of the Buddha's knowing and seeing—that's why they appear.
Normal: "Śāriputra, this is why the Buddhas appear in the world for one great matter, one great cause and condition."
Normal: The Buddha told Śāriputra: "The Buddhas, the Tathāgatas, they only teach and transform bodhisattvas. Everything they do, it's always for this one matter. They only use the Buddha's knowing and seeing to show and awaken living beings.
Normal: "Śāriputra, the Tathāgata, he only teaches dharma to living beings using the One Buddha Vehicle. There ain't no other vehicles—not two, not three.
Normal: "Śāriputra, the dharma of all the Buddhas in all ten directions—it's like this too."
Heading 2: THE THREE TIMES—PAST, FUTURE, PRESENT
Normal: "Śāriputra, them Buddhas of the past, they used countless, numberless skillful means—all kinds of causes, all kinds of comparisons, all kinds of expressions—to teach dharma for living beings. All them dharmas was for the sake of the One Buddha Vehicle. All them living beings who heard the dharma from the Buddhas—in the end, they all obtained the wisdom of all modes.
Normal: "Śāriputra, them Buddhas of the future, when they gonna appear in the world, they also gonna use countless, numberless skillful means—all kinds of causes, all kinds of comparisons, all kinds of expressions—to teach dharma for living beings. All them dharmas gonna be for the sake of the One Buddha Vehicle. All them living beings who hear the dharma from the Buddhas—in the end, they all gonna obtain the wisdom of all modes.
Normal: "Śāriputra, right now, in the countless hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of Buddha-lands throughout the ten directions, them Buddhas, them World-Honored Ones, they benefiting and bringing peace to living beings in so many ways. These Buddhas too, they using countless, numberless skillful means—all kinds of causes, all kinds of comparisons, all kinds of expressions—to teach dharma for living beings. All them dharmas is for the sake of the One Buddha Vehicle. All them living beings who hear the dharma from the Buddhas—in the end, they all gonna obtain the wisdom of all modes.
Normal: "Śāriputra, these Buddhas, they only teach and transform bodhisattvas. They want to show living beings the Buddha's knowing and seeing. They want to awaken living beings to the Buddha's knowing and seeing. They want to cause living beings to enter the Buddha's knowing and seeing.
Normal: "Śāriputra, I'm the same way right now too. I know living beings got all kinds of desires. Deep in their minds, they attached to things. Following their original natures, using all kinds of causes, all kinds of comparisons, all kinds of expressions, the power of skillful means—I speak the dharma for them.
Normal: "Śāriputra, all this—it's all for the sake of obtaining the One Buddha Vehicle and the wisdom of all modes."
Heading 2: ONLY ONE VEHICLE—THE BUDDHA VEHICLE
Normal: "Śāriputra, in the worlds of the ten directions, there ain't even two vehicles, much less three.
Normal: "Śāriputra, when the Buddhas appear in a world of five kinds of defilement—the defilement of the age, the defilement of afflictions, the defilement of living beings, the defilement of views, the defilement of lifespan—when it's like that, Śāriputra, when the age is all disturbed and chaotic, living beings heavy with filth, stingy and jealous, accomplishing roots of unwholesomeness, the Buddhas use the power of skillful means. Within the One Buddha Vehicle, they make distinctions and speak of three.
Normal: "Śāriputra, if my disciples call themselves arhats or solitary-walkers, but they don't hear, don't know that the Buddhas, the Tathāgatas, only teach and transform bodhisattvas—these ain't disciples of the Buddha. They ain't arhats. They ain't solitary-walkers.
Normal: "Furthermore, Śāriputra, them monks and nuns who say they already obtained arhatship, say they in their final body, say they reached ultimate nirvāṇa—and then they don't keep seeking anuttara-samyak-sambodhi no more—you ought to know that folks like this, they all arrogant people.
Normal: "And why's that? If there's a monk who truly obtained arhatship, and he don't believe this dharma—that situation don't exist. Except after the Buddha's extinction, when there ain't no Buddha present in the world. And why's that? After the Buddha's extinction, sutras like this—folks who can accept and uphold them, read and recite them, understand their meaning—them kind of people is hard to find. If they meet another Buddha later on, concerning this dharma, they gonna obtain complete understanding.
Normal: "Śāriputra, all of you ought to single-mindedly believe, understand, accept and uphold the Buddha's words. The words of the Buddhas, the Tathāgatas—they ain't false. There ain't no other vehicle. There's only the One Buddha Vehicle."
Heading 2: VERSES ON THE FIVE THOUSAND AND THE ONE VEHICLE
Normal: Monks and nuns
Normal: Full up with arrogance,
Normal: Laymen puffed up with pride,
Normal: Laywomen who don't believe—
Normal: Four kinds of folks like these,
Normal: Five thousand in their number.
Normal: They don't see their own faults,
Normal: They got shortcomings in keeping precepts,
Normal: Protecting and cherishing their own flaws.
Normal: These small-minded ones done left,
Normal: The chaff and the husks of the assembly—
Normal: Through the Buddha's awesome virtue they gone.
Normal: These folks got scarce merit and virtue,
Normal: They ain't capable of receiving this dharma.
Normal: This assembly now ain't got no branches and leaves,
Normal: It's only got them genuine and real.
Normal: Śāriputra, listen well now:
Normal: The dharma that the Buddhas obtained—
Normal: Using measureless skillful power,
Normal: They speak it out for living beings.
Normal: The minds of living beings and what they thinking,
Normal: The various roads they walking,
Normal: All their different desire-natures,
Normal: Their good and bad karma from previous lives—
Normal: The Buddha knows all this completely.
Normal: Using causes and comparisons,
Normal: Expressions and the power of skillful means,
Normal: He makes everybody rejoice.
Normal: Sometimes he speaks sutras,
Normal: Gathas and past events,
Normal: Birth stories and unprecedented things.
Normal: He also speaks about causes and conditions,
Normal: Comparisons and geyas too,
Normal: And the upadesa sutras.
Normal: Them dull-rooted folks who love the small dharma,
Normal: Greedy and attached to birth and death,
Normal: Concerning all them countless Buddhas,
Normal: They don't walk the deep and wonderful road.
Normal: Disturbed and troubled by all kinds of suffering,
Normal: For them I speak about nirvāṇa.
Normal: I set up these skillful means
Normal: To lead them into the Buddha's wisdom.
Normal: I never said to any of you
Normal: That you gonna accomplish the Buddha-road.
Normal: The reason I never said it—
Normal: The time to say it hadn't arrived yet.
Normal: But now is exactly the right time
Normal: To decisively speak the Great Vehicle.
Normal: These nine divisions of my dharma,
Normal: I speak them according to what living beings need.
Normal: They leading into the Great Vehicle—that's the fundamental reason—
Normal: And that's why I speak this sutra.
Normal: There's Buddha-children with pure minds,
Normal: Gentle and also sharp-rooted,
Normal: Who at the place of countless Buddhas
Normal: Done walked the deep and wonderful road.
Normal: For these Buddha-children here,
Normal: I speak this Great Vehicle sutra.
Normal: I predict that folks like these,
Normal: In lives to come, gonna accomplish the Buddha-road.
Normal: Because with deep minds they remember the Buddha,
Normal: Practice and uphold the pure precepts.
Normal: When these folks hear they gonna become Buddhas,
Normal: Great joy fills up their whole body.
Normal: The Buddha knows the way their minds moving,
Normal: And so for them he speaks the Great Vehicle.
Normal: When disciples or bodhisattvas
Normal: Hear the dharma that I speak,
Normal: Even just a single verse—
Normal: They all gonna become Buddhas, no doubt about it.
Normal: In all them Buddha-lands of the ten directions,
Normal: There's only the dharma of one vehicle,
Normal: Not two and not three neither.
Normal: Except when the Buddha uses skillful means—
Normal: Just using temporary, provisional names and words
Normal: To lead and guide living beings,
Normal: Speaking about the Buddha's wisdom.
Normal: When Buddhas appear in the world,
Normal: It's only for this one true matter—
Normal: Them other two ain't real.
Normal: The Buddha will never use the Small Vehicle
Normal: To ferry living beings across.
Normal: The Buddha himself dwells in the Great Vehicle,
Normal: And according to the dharma he obtained—
Normal: Concentration and wisdom for his adornment—
Normal: With this he ferries living beings across.
Normal: Having himself realized the unsurpassed road,
Normal: The Great Vehicle dharma, equal for all—
Normal: If I was to use the Small Vehicle
Normal: To teach even one single person,
Normal: I'd be falling into stinginess and greed—
Normal: This matter would be impossible.
Normal: If a person has faith and takes refuge in the Buddha,
Normal: The Tathāgata don't deceive or cheat,
Normal: Don't have no greedy or jealous intention,
Normal: Cut off all evil among the dharmas.
Normal: Therefore, the Buddha in the ten directions—
Normal: He alone is without any fear.
Normal: I use these marks to adorn my body,
Normal: My light shines throughout the world.
Normal: Honored by measureless multitudes,
Normal: I speak the seal of true reality.
Normal: Śāriputra, you ought to know—
Normal: Originally I made this vow:
Normal: Wanting to cause all living beings
Normal: To be equal to me, no different.
Normal: Like the vow I made long ago,
Normal: Now it's already completely fulfilled.
Normal: I'm transforming all living beings,
Normal: Causing them all to enter the Buddha-road.
Normal: If I meet living beings
Normal: And teach them all about the Buddha-road—
Normal: Them without wisdom would get confused and lost,
Normal: Deluded, they wouldn't receive the teaching.
Normal: I know these living beings here,
Normal: They never cultivated wholesome roots before.
Normal: They firmly attached to the five desires,
Normal: Through ignorance and craving they born troubled.
Normal: Through all their desire causes and conditions,
Normal: They fall down into the three evil paths,
Normal: Revolving through the six destinies,
Normal: Fully receiving every kind of suffering and poison.
Normal: The tiny form when they conceived,
Normal: World after world it keeps on growing.
Normal: People with thin virtue and little merit,
Normal: Oppressed and forced by all kinds of suffering,
Normal: They enter into a dense forest of wrong views—
Normal: Either existence or non-existence and such like.
Normal: Depending on these various views,
Normal: Complete with sixty-two of them,
Normal: Deeply attached to false and empty dharmas,
Normal: Firmly grasping them, can't let them go.
Normal: Arrogant, bragging on themselves,
Normal: Crooked and flattering, their minds not real.
Normal: For thousands of millions of billions of ages
Normal: They don't even hear the Buddha's name,
Normal: Don't hear the proper dharma neither—
Normal: Folks like this is hard to ferry across.
Normal: That's why, Śāriputra,
Normal: I set up skillful means for them,
Normal: Speaking about all them roads that end suffering,
Normal: Showing them nirvāṇa.
Normal: Even though I speak nirvāṇa,
Normal: This also ain't true extinction.
Normal: All the dharmas from the very beginning,
Normal: They always had the mark of still extinction.
Normal: When Buddha-children finish walking the road,
Normal: In lives to come they gonna become Buddhas.
Normal: I got this skillful power,
Normal: I open up and show the dharma of three vehicles.
Normal: All them World-Honored Ones,
Normal: They all speak the road of one vehicle.
Normal: Now this whole great assembly here,
Normal: All ought to get rid of their doubt and wondering.
Normal: The Buddhas' words don't differ none—
Normal: There's only one, not two vehicles.
Normal: In the past, countless ages back,
Normal: Measureless extinct Buddhas,
Normal: Hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of kinds,
Normal: Their number beyond all measuring—
Normal: World-Honored Ones like these,
Normal: Using various causes and comparisons,
Normal: Countless powers of skillful means,
Normal: They taught and explained the marks of the dharmas.
Normal: All these World-Honored Ones,
Normal: They all spoke the dharma of one vehicle,
Normal: Transformed measureless living beings,
Normal: Caused them to enter the Buddha-road.
Normal: Also, them Great Holy Lords,
Normal: Knowing the entire world—
Normal: Heavenly beings, human beings, every kind of living creature—
Normal: The deep desires of their minds—
Normal: They used different skillful means
Normal: To help reveal the foremost meaning.
Normal: If there was living creatures
Normal: Who met them Buddhas of the past,
Normal: Whether they heard dharma or gave gifts,
Normal: Or upheld precepts, practiced patience,
Normal: Vigor, meditation, wisdom, and such—
Normal: Cultivating merit and wisdom in various ways—
Normal: Folks like these,
Normal: They all done already accomplished the Buddha-road.
Normal: After the Buddhas became extinct,
Normal: If people had good, gentle hearts,
Normal: Living beings like these,
Normal: They all done already accomplished the Buddha-road.
Normal: After the Buddhas became extinct,
Normal: Those who made offerings to the relics—
Normal: Raised up millions and billions of kinds of stupas,
Normal: Made from gold and silver and crystal,
Normal: Mother-of-pearl and agate,
Normal: Rose quartz and lapis lazuli pearls,

Normal: Decorating all them stupas.
Normal: Or some raised up stone temples,
Normal: Sandalwood and agarwood,

Normal: Brick and tile, clay and earth.
Normal: If in some wilderness place
Normal: They heaped up dirt to make a Buddha-shrine,
Normal: Or even children playing,
Normal: Piling up sand to make a Buddha-stupa—
Normal: Folks like these,
Normal: They all done already accomplished the Buddha-road.
Normal: If people for the Buddha's sake
Normal: Established all kinds of images,
Normal: Carved and sculpted with every kind of mark—
Normal: They all done already accomplished the Buddha-road.
Normal: Whether made from seven jewels,
Normal: Bronze or red and white copper,
Normal: White pewter, lead and tin,
Normal: Iron, wood, or even clay,
Normal: Or using glue and lacquer and cloth
Normal: To adorn and make Buddha-images—
Normal: Folks like these,
Normal: They all done already accomplished the Buddha-road.
Normal: Painting and drawing Buddha-images,
Normal: Complete with a hundred merits adorning the marks,
Normal: Whether they did it themselves or had others do it—
Normal: They all done already accomplished the Buddha-road.
Normal: Even children playing,
Normal: Using grass or wood or a brush,
Normal: Or maybe even fingernails
Normal: To scratch and draw a Buddha-image—
Normal: Folks like these,
Normal: Gradually accumulating merit and virtue,
Normal: Completely fulfilling great compassion-mind—
Normal: They all done already accomplished the Buddha-road.
Normal: They only teaching and transforming bodhisattvas,
Normal: Ferrying across measureless multitudes.
Normal: If people at stupas and temples,
Normal: At jeweled images or painted images,
Normal: With flowers, incense, banners, canopies,
Normal: Made offerings with reverent minds—
Normal: If they had people make music,
Normal: Beating drums, blowing horns and conches,

Normal: All these wonderful sounds,
Normal: Playing them all as offerings—
Normal: Or with joyful minds
Normal: Singing and chanting the Buddha's virtue,
Normal: Even just one small sound—
Normal: They all done already accomplished the Buddha-road.
Normal: If people with distracted minds,
Normal: Even just with a single flower,
Normal: Made an offering to a painted image—
Normal: Gradually they gonna see countless Buddhas.
Normal: Or some people bowed in respect,
Normal: Or maybe just pressed their palms together,
Normal: Or even just raised one hand,

Normal: By making offerings to images like this,
Normal: Gradually they gonna see measureless Buddhas.

Normal: Extensively ferry across numberless multitudes,
Normal: Enter nirvāṇa without remainder,
Normal: Like firewood exhausted, fire gone out.
Normal: If people with distracted minds
Normal: Enter into a stupa or temple,
Normal: One time call out 'Homage to the Buddha!'—
Normal: They all done already accomplished the Buddha-road.
Normal: Concerning all them Buddhas of the past,
Normal: Whether while they was in the world or after they extinct—
Normal: If there's folks who heard this dharma,
Normal: They all done already accomplished the Buddha-road.
Normal: All them World-Honored Ones of the future,
Normal: Their number without any measure—
Normal: All these Tathāgatas
Normal: Gonna use skillful means to speak the dharma.
Normal: All the Tathāgatas,
Normal: Using measureless skillful means,
Normal: Gonna ferry living beings across,
Normal: Cause them to enter the Buddha's wisdom without outflow.
Normal: If there's folks who hear the dharma,
Normal: Not a single one won't become a Buddha.
Normal: The Buddhas' original vow and wish was:
Normal: 'The Buddha-road that I'm walking—
Normal: I want to cause living beings universally
Normal: To obtain this same road too.'
Normal: The Buddhas of the future world,
Normal: Even though they gonna speak hundreds of thousands of billions,

Normal: Actually it's for the one vehicle.
Normal: The Buddhas, Honored Ones of Two Feet,
Normal: They know the dharma constantly has no nature—
Normal: Buddha-seed arises from conditions—
Normal: That's why they speak the one vehicle.
Normal: This dharma dwells in the dharma-position,
Normal: The worldly marks constantly abide.
Normal: Having known this at the place of awakening,
Normal: The Guide uses skillful means to speak.
Normal: The heavenly beings and humans who make offerings,
Normal: The present Buddhas of the ten directions,
Normal: Numerous as Ganges River sands,

Normal: For the sake of bringing peace to living beings,
Normal: They also speak dharma like this.
Normal: Knowing the foremost still extinction,
Normal: Using the power of skillful means,
Normal: Although they showing various roads,
Normal: Actually it's for the Buddha Vehicle.

Normal: What's thought deep in their minds,
Normal: Their karma practiced in the past,
Normal: Their desire-natures, vigor-power,
Normal: And whether their faculties sharp or dull—
Normal: Using various causes and conditions,
Normal: Comparisons and also expressions,
Normal: They speak with appropriate skillful means.
Normal: Now I'm the same way too—
Normal: For the sake of bringing peace to living beings,
Normal: Using various dharma-doors,
Normal: I'm proclaiming and showing the Buddha-road.
Normal: With my power of wisdom,
Normal: I know living beings' natures and desires.
Normal: Using skillful means, speaking all the dharmas,
Normal: I'm causing them all to gain joy.
Normal: Śāriputra, you ought to know—
Normal: With my Buddha-eye I'm looking,
Normal: Seeing living beings of the six paths,
Normal: Poor and without merit or wisdom,
Normal: Entering the dangerous road of birth and death,
Normal: Suffering continuing on without break,
Normal: Deeply attached to the five desires,
Normal: Like a yak loving its tail—
Normal: With greed and craving they damaging themselves,
Normal: Blind in the darkness, can't see nothing.
Normal: They don't seek the Buddha with his great might,
Normal: Don't seek the dharma that cuts off suffering neither.
Normal: Deep into all kinds of wrong views they go,
Normal: Trying to use suffering to get rid of suffering.
Normal: For the sake of living beings like these,
Normal: I arise with a great compassion-mind.
Normal: When I first sat at the place of awakening,
Normal: Gazing at the tree and also walking,
Normal: For three times seven days
Normal: I thought about matters like this:
Normal: 'The wisdom I obtained—
Normal: It's subtle, wonderful, most foremost.
Normal: Living beings got dull faculties,
Normal: Attached to pleasure, blinded by ignorance.
Normal: Folks like these here—
Normal: How can they possibly be ferried across?'
Normal: At that time, all them Brahma kings
Normal: And all them Lord Shakras too,
Normal: The Four Heavenly Kings protecting the world,
Normal: And the Great Freedom Heaven god,
Normal: Along with other hosts of heavenly beings,
Normal: Retinues of hundreds of thousands of millions,
Normal: Respectfully with palms pressed together, bowing,
Normal: They begged me to turn the dharma-wheel.
Normal: I immediately thought to myself:
Normal: 'If I only praise the Buddha Vehicle,
Normal: Living beings sunk down in suffering,
Normal: They won't be able to believe this dharma.
Normal: Because they break the dharma and don't believe,
Normal: They gonna fall into the three evil paths.
Normal: I'd rather not speak the dharma at all,
Normal: Just quickly enter into nirvāṇa.'
Normal: Then I remembered them Buddhas of the past,
Normal: The power of skillful means they practiced.

Normal: I also ought to speak three vehicles.'
Normal: While I was thinking like this,
Normal: Buddhas from the ten directions all appeared.

Normal: Following all the Buddhas everywhere,
Normal: You gonna use the power of skillful means.
Normal: We too all obtained
Normal: The most wonderful, foremost dharma.

Normal: That's why, using skillful means,
Normal: We make distinctions and speak about various fruits.

Normal: It's only for teaching bodhisattvas.'
Normal: Śāriputra, you ought to know—
Normal: I heard them holy lion-roars,
Normal: Their deep, pure, subtle, wonderful sounds,
Normal: Joyfully calling 'Homage to the Buddha!'
Normal: Then I thought like this:
Normal: 'I came out into this defiled, evil world.
Normal: Just like all them Buddhas spoke,
Normal: I also ought to follow and practice accordingly.'
Normal: After I thought about this matter,
Normal: I immediately went to Varanasi.
Normal: The marks of the dharmas—still extinction—
Normal: Can't be proclaimed in words.
Normal: Using the power of skillful means,
Normal: For five monks I spoke it.
Normal: This is called turning the dharma-wheel.
Normal: Then there was the sound of nirvāṇa,
Normal: And also 'arhat,'
Normal: And 'dharma' and 'sangha'—these distinguishing names.
Normal: From ages long ago till now,
Normal: I been praising the dharma of nirvāṇa—
Normal: The suffering of birth and death forever exhausted—
Normal: I always speak like this.
Normal: Śāriputra, you ought to know:
Normal: I see them Buddha-children,
Normal: Ones aspiring and seeking the Buddha-road,
Normal: Countless thousands of millions of billions.
Normal: All with reverent minds,
Normal: They come to where the Buddha is.
Normal: They done heard from all them Buddhas before
Normal: Dharma spoken with skillful means.
