They'll bow down and honor that wonderful seven-jeweled tower.
Normal: "Countless beings will attain arhat-fruit. Countless beings will awaken to the pratyekabuddha way. Inconceivable numbers of beings will bring forth the enlightenment mind and reach non-regression."
Normal: The Buddha tells all the monks:
Normal: "In a future age, if there are good men or good women who hear this Devadatta Chapter of the Wonderful Dharma Lotus Sutra, and they believe it with pure hearts, respect it, don't doubt it—they won't fall into hell, won't fall into the realm of hungry ghosts, won't fall into the animal realm.
Normal: "They'll be born right there in front of buddhas in the ten directions. Wherever they're born, they'll always be hearing this sutra.
Normal: "If they're born among humans or devas, they'll receive supremely wonderful happiness.
Normal: "If they're born in the presence of a buddha, they'll be born by transformation from a lotus flower."
Normal: Right then, Wisdom-Accumulation Bodhisattva—the one who came with Many Treasures World-Honored One from below—he says to Many Treasures Buddha:
Normal: "We should return to our homeland now."
Normal: But Śākyamuni Buddha tells Wisdom-Accumulation:
Normal: "Good son, wait a little while, just a little bit. There's a bodhisattva here named Mañjuśrī—Wonderful Virtue. You should meet him. You should talk with him about the wonderful Dharma. Then you can return to your homeland."
Normal: And right at that moment, Mañjuśrī is sitting on a thousand-petaled lotus flower, big as a chariot wheel. And the bodhisattvas who came with him are also sitting on jeweled lotus flowers. They rise up naturally from the great ocean, from the palace of Sāgara the Dragon King. They come up, suspended in empty space. They go to Vulture Peak Mountain. They step down from their lotus flowers and go to where the Buddha is. They bow their heads to the ground, honoring the feet of both World-Honored Ones—both buddhas sitting there. When they finish paying respects, they go to where Wisdom-Accumulation is sitting. They exchange greetings, ask how each other is doing. Then they sit down to one side.
Normal: Wisdom-Accumulation Bodhisattva asks Mañjuśrī:
Normal: "You went to the dragon palace. How many beings did you teach down there? How many did you convert?"
Normal: Mañjuśrī says:
Normal: "The number is immeasurable. Can't count them. Can't calculate them. Can't speak it with the mouth. Can't measure it with the mind. Just wait a little while. You'll have your proof. You'll see for yourself."
Normal: Before he even finishes speaking, countless bodhisattvas sitting on jeweled lotus flowers come rising up from the ocean. They come to Vulture Peak Mountain and stay there, suspended in empty space.
Normal: All these bodhisattvas were taught and transformed by Mañjuśrī. They've all accomplished the bodhisattva practices. They're all discussing the six perfections together.
Normal: The ones who used to be śrāvakas, hearers—they're up there in empty space, but they're teaching the śrāvaka practices. But now they're all practicing the emptiness teaching of the great vehicle.
Normal: Mañjuśrī says to Wisdom-Accumulation:
Normal: "The teaching and transforming I did in the ocean—it went like this. That's what happened."
Normal: Then Wisdom-Accumulation Bodhisattva speaks in verse to praise him:
Normal: You have great wisdom, virtue, courage, strength—
Normal: You've taught and transformed countless beings, great length.
Normal: Now this great assembly and I have all seen
Normal: The real characteristics expounded, what they mean.
Normal: You've revealed the one vehicle Dharma, opened it clear,
Normal: You've guided all living beings, brought them near.
Normal: You help them quickly achieve the enlightenment way—
Normal: That's what you've been doing, night and day.
Normal: Mañjuśrī says:
Normal: "When I was in the ocean, I only kept teaching the Wonderful Dharma Lotus Sutra. Nothing else. Just this."
Normal: Wisdom-Accumulation asks Mañjuśrī:
Normal: "This sutra is so deep, so subtle, so wonderful. It's the treasure of all sutras. It's rare in the world. Is there any living being who practiced this sutra diligently, put real effort into it, and quickly became a buddha? Tell me—did that happen?"
Normal: Mañjuśrī says:
Normal: "There's the daughter of Sāgara the Dragon King. She just turned eight years old. Eight! But she's got sharp wisdom, keen intelligence. She understands all the roots and karmic actions of living beings. She's got dhāraṇī. She can receive and hold all the deep secret treasures taught by the buddhas—every word, she holds it.
Normal: "She's entered deep into meditation. She thoroughly understands all dharmas. In the space of an instant—one moment—she brought forth the enlightenment mind. She reached non-regression. Her eloquence has no obstruction, no barrier.
Normal: "She thinks of living beings with compassion, like they're her own children. Her merit and virtue are complete. When she thinks something in her mind, when she speaks it with her mouth, it's subtle, wonderful, vast, and great. She's compassionate, humane, yielding, gentle. Her will and spirit are harmonious and refined.
Normal: "She can reach enlightenment. She can arrive at bodhi."
Normal: Wisdom-Accumulation Bodhisattva says:
Normal: "I've seen Śākyamuni Tathāgata. For immeasurable kalpas he practiced difficult and bitter practices. He accumulated merit, piled up virtue, seeking the bodhisattva way. He never stopped, not even for a moment. I look at this great thousand-world system—every part of it, down to a space as small as a mustard seed—there's not one spot that's not a place where the Bodhisattva gave up his body and life for the sake of living beings. Only after all that did he achieve the enlightenment way.
Normal: "I don't believe this girl, in just a brief instant, could achieve perfect enlightenment. Can't believe it."
Normal: Before he even finishes speaking, the dragon king's daughter suddenly appears right there in front of them. She bows, touching her head to the ground in respect, then stands to one side. She speaks in verse to praise the Buddha:
Normal: You deeply understand the marks of sin and merit,
Normal: You illuminate the ten directions—all can hear it.
Normal: Your subtle, wonderful, pure dharma body, so sublime,
Normal: Has the thirty-two marks, perfect in every sign.
Normal: The eighty minor characteristics adorn the dharma body bright,
Normal: Honored by devas and humans, worshipped day and night.
Normal: Dragons and spirits all bow down with respect—
Normal: Every kind of living being honors you, every sect.
Normal: I've also heard you've achieved the enlightenment way,
Normal: Only a buddha can bear witness to this, I say.
Normal: I'm revealing the great vehicle teaching, opening it wide,
Normal: To rescue suffering beings on every side.
Normal: Right then, Śāriputra speaks to the dragon girl and says:
Normal: "You say you're about to quickly attain supreme enlightenment? But that's hard to believe. Can't be trusted. Why not?
Normal: "A woman's body is filthy, impure. It's not a vessel for the Dharma. How could you attain supreme enlightenment?
Normal: "The buddha-way is so vast, so far away! You have to practice through immeasurable kalpas, endure bitterness, pile up practices, perfect all the perfections. Only then do you succeed.
Normal: "Plus, a woman's body has five obstacles. What are they?
Normal: "First, she can't become a Brahma Heaven King.
Normal: "Second, she can't become Indra.
Normal: "Third, she can't become Mara, the demon king.
Normal: "Fourth, she can't become a wheel-turning sage king.
Normal: "Fifth, she can't become a buddha.
Normal: "So how could a woman's body quickly achieve buddhahood? Can't happen."
Normal: Right then the dragon girl had a precious jewel, worth as much as a great thousand-world system—worth three thousand great thousand worlds. She held it up and presented it to the Buddha.
Normal: The Buddha received it immediately.
Normal: The dragon girl said to Wisdom-Accumulation Bodhisattva and to the Venerable Śāriputra:
Normal: "I presented a precious jewel, and the World-Honored One accepted it. Was that quick or not?"
Normal: They answered: "Very quick!"
Normal: The girl said:
Normal: "Use your spiritual power. Watch me become a buddha. It's gonna be even faster than that."
Normal: Right at that moment, everyone in the assembly saw the dragon girl suddenly—in an instant—transform into a male. She perfected the bodhisattva practices. Immediately she went south to the Spotless World. She sat down on a jeweled lotus flower and achieved perfect, complete enlightenment. She had the thirty-two marks. She had the eighty minor characteristics. She taught the wonderful Dharma for all living beings throughout the ten directions.
Normal: At that time, in this Saha world—all the bodhisattvas, śrāvakas, the eight classes of devas and dragons, humans and non-humans—they all saw from far away that dragon girl becoming a buddha, teaching the Dharma to all the devas and humans gathered at that time.
Normal: Their hearts filled up with great joy. They all bowed in reverence from a distance.
Normal: Countless living beings heard the Dharma, understood it, awakened to it. They attained non-regression.
Normal: Countless living beings received prophecies of their future enlightenment.
Normal: The Spotless World shook in six ways.
Normal: Three thousand living beings in this Saha world reached the ground of non-regression. Three thousand living beings brought forth the enlightenment mind and received prophecies.
Normal: Wisdom-Accumulation Bodhisattva, the Venerable Śāriputra, and the whole assembly—they all silently believed and accepted this.
Normal: END OF CHAPTER TWELVE: WHEN YOUR ENEMY WAS YOUR TEACHER
Heading 2: INTERPRETATION NOTES:
Normal: This is Chapter 12 of the Wonderful Dharma Lotus Sutra, translated from Kumārajīva's Classical Chinese (406 CE) into blues/gospel vernacular English.
Normal: This chapter carries one of the most revolutionary messages in the entire sutra: that enlightenment is immediate and available to all, regardless of social barriers. The Buddha reveals that Devadatta—his cousin who tried to kill him, who split the sangha, who is in hell for his crimes—was actually his greatest teacher. Through opposition and resistance, Devadatta pushed the Buddha toward complete awakening.
Normal: Then comes the dragon princess—an eight-year-old girl, non-human, doubly excluded by the "five obstacles" doctrine—who demonstrates instant enlightenment right there in front of everyone who said it was impossible.
Normal: Key metaphors in this interpretation:
Normal: "Your Enemy Was Your Teacher"
Normal: - The chapter title captures the radical teaching that life's hardest trials and greatest opponents can be our deepest educators. This resonates with the blues tradition's understanding that suffering teaches, that the hard road makes you wise.
Normal: The King Becoming a Servant
Normal: - I rendered the Buddha's past-life story of royal power surrendered for truth as a blues narrative of status reversed: "I was a king / Had everything a man could want." This mirrors the gospel theme of the last being first, the high brought low.
Normal: "Watch how fast this is"
Normal: - The dragon princess's challenge becomes vernacular direct speech, the kind of thing someone would actually say before demonstrating impossible grace.
Normal: Instant transformation
Normal: - The sudden shift from female to male to enlightened buddha happens "right at that moment," "in an instant," "suddenly"—language of the spontaneous grace moment central to gospel testimony, when everything changes in the blink of an eye.
Normal: This chapter is about barriers broken, impossibilities made possible, enemies revealed as friends, and the instantaneous nature of awakening—themes that resonate deeply with the African American spiritual tradition's understanding of liberation, reversal, and sudden grace.
Heading 1: CHAPTER THIRTEEN: WHEN THE ROAD GETS ROUGH, YOU GOTTA KEEP WALKING

Heading 2: THE FIRST VOW - MEDICINE KING AND GREAT JOY STEP FORWARD
Normal: Now at that time, Medicine King Bodhisattva and Great Joy in Preaching Bodhisattva—these two great souls—they stood up together with twenty thousand of their brother and sister bodhisattvas. They all gathered right there in front of the Buddha, and they made a promise, you hear me, they made a VOW:
Normal: "World-Honored One, don't you worry yourself none. Don't let your mind be troubled about what's coming. When you gone from this world, when you passed on to the other shore, WE gonna be here. We gonna hold this teaching. We gonna read it, recite it, explain it, and live it out.
Normal: "Now we know—Lord, we KNOW—that the times coming after you leave gonna be dark times, evil times. The people gonna have less and less good roots growing in their hearts. They gonna be full up with pride, puffed up like balloons thinking they somebody special. They gonna be hungry for profit, greedy for respect, chasing after offerings and honors. They gonna feed the wrong seeds in their souls, and they gonna be far, far away from freedom.
Normal: "Teaching them gonna be like trying to get water from a stone. It's gonna be HARD. But we making a promise right here, right now: We gonna raise up a GREAT PATIENCE inside ourselves. We gonna read this sutra, hold it, speak it, write it down, and honor it every way we can. And we ain't gonna hold back. We ain't gonna spare our bodies. We ain't gonna count the cost. Even if it take our very lives—we gonna carry this teaching forward."

Normal: "World-Honored One, we gonna go to other lands too. We gonna spread this sutra far and wide in those places.

Normal: "So we taking this teaching somewhere else, where maybe folks got a chance to hear it clean."
Heading 2: THE BUDDHA'S AUNT GETS HER PROPHECY
Normal: Now at that time, the Buddha's aunt—her name was Mahāprajāpatī, and she was a nun, a bhikṣuṇī—she stood up together with six thousand other nuns, some still learning and some done with learning. They all rose from their seats as one, pressed their palms together, and they looked up at the Blessed One's face. They looked at him with their whole hearts, couldn't take their eyes off him, not even for a second.
Normal: And the World-Honored One, he saw that look on her face and he said to her:

You thinking maybe I ain't said your name? You thinking maybe I ain't given you your prophecy of supreme, perfect enlightenment—anuttara-samyak-sambodhi?"
Normal: And then Buddha said:
Normal: "Gautamī, listen here. When I spoke before about ALL the voice-hearers getting their prophecy, you was INCLUDED in that, you hear me? But now, if you want to know the particulars, if you want to know YOUR specific name and YOUR specific promise, then listen:
Normal: "In the world that's coming, you gonna be a GREAT DHARMA TEACHER in the Dharma of sixty-eight thousand billion Buddhas. Count them—SIXTY-EIGHT THOUSAND BILLION! And these six thousand nuns with you, still learning and done with learning, they gonna be Dharma teachers right alongside you.
Normal: "And you gonna walk that Bodhisattva path step by step, gradually perfecting yourself, until you BECOME a Buddha yourself. Normal: "And Gautamī, when you become that Buddha—All-Beings-Rejoice-to-See Buddha—you and these six thousand bodhisattvas with you, y'all gonna take turns giving prophecies to each other, passing on the promise of supreme, perfect enlightenment from one to the next like a torch that never goes out."

Normal: These wasn't no beginners. These was bodhisattvas who CANNOT FALL BACK—avinivartanīya—they done passed the point of no return. They turn the wheel of no-retreating Dharma. They got all the dhāraṇīs, all the mystical formulas and powers.
Normal: These great souls, they rose up from their seats together and went before the Buddha. They pressed their palms together with one mind, one heart, and they thought to themselves:

Normal: "All of this gonna happen because of the BUDDHA'S POWER, the Buddha's authority and grace. So we asking you, World-Honored One: When you in other lands far away from here, WATCH OVER US from a distance. Guard us and protect us while we doing this work."
Normal: And then all these bodhisattvas together, with ONE VOICE, they broke out into verse. They sang out their vow, and this is what they sang:

Heading 2: INTERPRETATION NOTES:
Normal: This chapter is pure testimony—a series of sacred vows made by different groups of disciples, each pledging to carry the Dharma forward after Buddha's passing. The structure mirrors the call-and-response pattern of gospel testimony meetings, where individuals and groups stand up to declare their commitment.
Normal: Key Metaphorical Choices:
Normal: "Armor of patience"
Normal: - The Chinese 忍辱鎧 (rěnrù kǎi) becomes the central image of spiritual protection, rendered as something you "put on" like a soldier preparing for battle.
Normal: "Lion's roar"
Normal: - The Sanskrit siṃhanāda becomes "speaking with power and authority, ain't scared of nothing" - the fearless proclamation of truth.
Normal: "We don't love our own lives"
Normal: - This line echoes the martyr tradition in Christianity ("they loved not their lives unto death") while preserving the Buddhist teaching of non-attachment to the physical body.
Normal: "We the Buddha's messengers"
Normal: - This directly parallels the Christian concept of apostleship (Greek: apostolos = "one sent forth") while maintaining fidelity to the Chinese 世尊使 (messenger/envoy of the World-Honored One).
Normal: The verse section maintains the repetitive, rhythmic structure of the Chinese original while using blues-style repetition ("we gonna... we gonna...") to create oral momentum. The confrontation with corrupt monks becomes a classic blues theme: the authentic versus the fake, the true preacher versus the charlatan, those who genuinely suffer for the cause versus those who profit from religion.
Normal: The closing testimony—"The Buddha knows our hearts"—echoes both the Buddhist understanding of Buddha's omniscience and the gospel singer's assurance that "God knows my heart," creating a bridge between traditions without violating either one.
Normal: This interpretation preserves the profound seriousness of these vows while making them accessible through vernacular language that carries its own tradition of suffering, endurance, and sacred commitment.
Heading 1: CHAPTER FOURTEEN: HOW TO KEEP YOUR SOUL CLEAN WHEN THE WORLD'S GONE WRONG
Normal: A Blues Interpretation from the Classical Chinese
Heading 2: MAÑJUŚRĪ ASKS THE HARD QUESTION
Normal: Now at that time, Mañjuśrī—that prince of the Dharma, that great bodhisattva—he stood up and said to the Buddha:
Normal: "World-Honored One, these bodhisattvas here, they're something rare, you know? They respect you so much they done made a vow—a big vow, a serious vow—that when the evil age comes rolling in, when everything's corrupt and wrong, they gonna protect this Lotus teaching. They gonna read it, study it, teach it out loud.
Normal: But World-Honored One, I got to ask: When that evil age comes—and it's coming—how can these bodhisattvas teach this sutra without losing themselves? How they gonna speak the truth when lies run the world?"
Normal: And the Buddha said to Mañjuśrī:
Normal: "Listen now. If a bodhisattva wants to teach this sutra in the evil age to come, they got to rest themselves in four practices—four ways of being that keep you safe, keep you clean, keep you whole. The first one's about where you stand. The second's about who you stand with. You got to know your ground, and you got to know your company."
Heading 2: FIRST PRACTICE: THE GROUND YOU STAND ON
Normal: "Mañjuśrī, what do I mean by a bodhisattva's ground—their place to stand?
Normal: Listen: If you gonna teach in hard times, you got to dwell on the ground of patience. That means you gentle. You soft. You kind. You don't rush to anger, don't fly off the handle, don't let violence take root in your heart. You can't be jumping at every shadow, can't be scared of your own spirit.
Normal: And here's the deep part—listen close now: You don't cling to no ideas about the Dharma. You don't make the teaching into something you hold tight like property. No action, no grasping when it comes to spiritual things.
Normal: You look at everything according to its true nature. You see things as they really are—not what you want them to be, not what you fear they are, but what they truly are in their essence.
Normal: And you don't discriminate. You don't say 'this one's high, that one's low.' You don't divide reality into pieces and then fight over the pieces.
Normal: That's your ground. That's where you stand. On patience, on seeing clear, on letting things be what they are."
Heading 2: SECOND PRACTICE: WHO YOU DON'T RUN WITH
Normal: "Now Mañjuśrī, what do I mean by who you associate with—who you spend your time around?
Normal: Let me be plain: A bodhisattva teaching in evil times, they got to stay away from certain people. Not because you hate them—you got compassion for everybody—but because their energy will pull you down, will cloud your vision, will compromise your teaching.
Normal: Don't get close with kings and princes, with government officials and ministers, with the powerful and mighty. Power corrupts, and corrupt power corrupts faster. You can teach them if they come to you, but don't seek their favor, don't curry their approval, don't become their pet preacher.
Normal: Don't get tight with heretics and false teachers, with people teaching paths that lead nowhere, with those making up doctrines from their own confusion. Don't study worldly literature just to sound smart, don't get caught up in fancy words and clever arguments that go nowhere.
Normal: Don't go to violent entertainments—no wrestling matches, no fights, no games where people hurt each other for fun. Don't hang around places where violence is entertainment.
Normal: Don't associate with outcasts doing evil work—not the butchers, not the hunters, not the fishermen killing for profit. Not the people raising animals just to slaughter them. Not the people selling sex, selling bodies, selling what shouldn't be sold. These are hard livelihoods, bitter livelihoods, and you can't let that bitterness seep into your teaching.
Normal: And this is important—don't even get close with those monks and nuns who seeking their own little salvation, their own private enlightenment. Those śrāvakas content with their own liberation—don't live with them. If they come to you, teach them without expecting nothing back. But don't take up residence in their small vision.
Normal: Now about women—and this is practical wisdom for those times: Don't look at women with desire, don't smile showing all your teeth, don't display your body, don't get familiar with young women or widows or those confused about their own nature. Not because women are bad—no, no—but because desire will corrupt your teaching, will make people question your motives, will muddy the clear water of the Dharma.
Normal: Don't take on young disciples or little novices who you can't properly guide. Don't share teachers with those who might lead you astray.
Normal: Always love quiet places. Always be meditating, gathering your mind, keeping your spirit collected. Don't let yourself scatter like dust in the wind.
Normal: That's the first part of associations—who you don't run with."
Heading 2: SECOND PRACTICE, SECOND PART: THE GROUND OF EMPTINESS
Normal: "But there's a deeper part to this second practice, Mañjuśrī. It's not just about avoiding people. It's about understanding reality itself.
Normal: View all things—all dharmas, all phenomena—as empty according to their true nature. Empty like space is empty, not because there's nothing there, but because there's no fixed essence, no permanent self.
Normal: Things aren't twisted up wrong, aren't moving toward some goal, aren't retreating from some danger, aren't turning into something else. They just ARE, moment by moment, like space itself—no substance you can grab hold of.
Normal: All our talking about things—all our language and concepts—it all falls short. Nothing is being produced, nothing is arising fresh, nothing is starting up new.
Normal: No names capture it. No forms define it. Truth be told, there ain't nothing there to capture—nothing you can put your finger on and say 'this is it.'
Normal: Limitless it is. Boundless. Without obstacles or barriers.
Normal: We only talk about things because of causes and conditions, because of our confused, upside-down thinking. That's the only reason we say anything at all.
Normal: If you love to contemplate these truths—if you rest your mind in this understanding that everything is empty, fluid, free—that's the second ground for a bodhisattva. That's the second safe place to stand."

Heading 2: THIRD PRACTICE: HOW TO SPEAK AND WHAT TO HOLD IN YOUR HEART
Normal: "Now, Mañjuśrī, listen: After I'm gone, in the last age when the Dharma's dying out, if you want to teach this Lotus Sutra, you got to dwell in peaceful conduct.
Normal: Whether you're speaking it out loud or reading it quiet, don't talk bad about people and their failings. Don't speak about what's wrong with other sutras.
Normal: Don't look down on other teachers of the Dharma. Don't gossip about people's good points and bad points, their strengths and their shortcomings.
Normal: When it comes to those śrāvakas—those seeking their own enlightenment—don't call them out by name to shame them. Don't name them to praise them either. Don't breed resentment in your heart.
Normal: If you cultivate this peaceful mind, if you practice this kind of speaking, then people who come to hear you won't turn against you. And when they ask you hard questions, don't answer with small teachings—don't give them the little vehicle. Answer with the great vehicle, with the big vision that leads to complete wisdom, to knowing all that can be known."
Normal: The bodhisattva always loves
Normal: to teach in peace and safety.
Normal: They prepare a clean place,
Normal: set up a proper seat,
Normal: Anoint their body with oil,
Normal: wash off the dust and dirt,
Normal: put on fresh clean clothes—
Normal: clean outside and inside both.

Normal: and answer what they're asked.

Normal: if officials and common people gather,
Normal: They teach with subtle meaning,
Normal: with a gentle face and kind words.

Normal: they answer according to the meaning.
Normal: They use causes and conditions,
Normal: they use parables and stories,
Normal: They explain and distinguish,
Normal: break it down so folks can understand.

Normal: everyone's inspired,
Normal: Gradually they increase,
Normal: gradually they enter the Buddha Way.

Normal: "I teach for this reason only:
Normal: so I can achieve Buddhahood,
Normal: so all beings can achieve it too."

Normal: That's your peaceful offering.
Normal: After I pass on,

Normal: this wondrous Lotus Sutra,

Normal: can't describe it with parables.
Heading 2: FOURTH PRACTICE: GREAT COMPASSION FOR THOSE WHO REJECT YOU
Normal: "Now, Mañjuśrī, there's one more practice—the fourth peaceful practice—for bodhisattvas teaching in the last age when the Dharma's dying out.
Normal: If you're teaching this Lotus Sutra, you got to keep your heart free from jealousy, from deceit, from lying. Don't look down on people learning the Buddha Way. Don't go searching for their faults.
Normal: Whether they're monks or nuns, laypeople, whether they're seeking the śrāvaka vehicle or the pratyekabuddha vehicle or the bodhisattva way—don't trouble them. Don't make them doubt themselves. Don't make them regret their path.
Normal: Don't say to them: 'You're far from the Way. You ain't never gonna reach complete knowledge. Why? Because you're lazy, that's why. Because you slack off on the path.'
Normal: And don't get into debates and arguments about the Dharma, don't get competitive about teaching.
Normal: Instead, toward all beings, generate great compassion. Toward all the Tathāgatas—all the Buddhas—hold them as loving fathers in your mind. Toward all the bodhisattvas, see them as your great teachers.
Normal: Toward the great bodhisattvas in all ten directions, always maintain deep respect in your heart. Bow down to them with reverence.
Normal: When you teach, teach all beings equally. Don't teach more to those who love the Dharma more. Don't measure out your teaching according to people's enthusiasm. Teach according to the Dharma itself—not too much, not too little, just what's right.
Normal: Even toward those who deeply love the teaching, don't give them extra just because they're eager."
Heading 2: THE FOURTH PRACTICE BRINGS PROTECTION AND COMMUNITY
Normal: "Mañjuśrī, if a bodhisattva in the last age—when the Dharma's dying—accomplishes this third peaceful practice, then when they teach this sutra, nobody can trouble them.
Normal: They'll find good companions to read and recite this sutra with them. They'll find large crowds coming to listen. And when people hear it, they'll be able to hold it. When they hold it, they'll be able to recite it. When they recite it, they'll be able to explain it. When they explain it, they'll be able to write it down, or get others to write it.
Normal: They'll make offerings to the sutra scroll, treat it with respect and honor, praise it and treasure it."
Normal: If you want to teach this sutra,
Normal: cast off jealousy and hatred and pride,
Normal: Cast off deceit and lying,
Normal: always practice straight honest conduct.
Normal: Don't look down on people,
Normal: don't argue about the Dharma,
Normal: Don't make others doubt and regret,
Normal: don't tell them they can't reach Buddhahood.
Normal: When this child of Buddha teaches,
Normal: they're always gentle, patient,
Normal: Compassionate to everyone,
Normal: never slacking off.
Normal: The great bodhisattvas of ten directions,
Normal: they practice the Way out of compassion—

Normal: say "These are my great teachers."

Normal: hold them as supreme fathers.
Normal: Break down your prideful heart
Normal: and you'll teach without obstruction.
Normal: This third practice is like this—
Normal: the wise should guard it well.
Normal: Single-heartedly dwell in peaceful practice
Normal: and countless people will respect you.
Heading 2: FOURTH PRACTICE: THE DEEPEST COMPASSION
Normal: "Now, Mañjuśrī, there's more to say about bodhisattvas in the last age when the Dharma's dying, those who hold this Lotus Sutra.
Normal: Toward those who've left home and those still in the household life, generate great compassion. Toward those who aren't bodhisattvas, generate even greater compassion—a vast compassion.
Normal: You should think like this: 'These people, they suffering a great loss. The Tathāgata teaches with skillful means according to what people need, but these folks—they don't hear it, don't know it, don't perceive it. They don't ask about it, don't believe it, don't understand it.
Normal: But even though they don't ask, don't believe, don't understand this sutra, when I reach complete perfect enlightenment, wherever they are, I'm gonna use my spiritual power and my wisdom power to draw them in, lead them here, make them dwell in this teaching.'
Normal: Mañjuśrī, if a bodhisattva after the Tathāgata passes on accomplishes this fourth practice, when they teach this sutra they won't make no mistakes, won't fall into error.
Normal: They'll always be honored by monks and nuns, by laymen and laywomen, by kings and princes, by government officials and common people, by priests and householders. They'll receive offerings, respect, honor, and praise.
Normal: The gods in the sky, wanting to hear the teaching, will constantly attend them. Whether they're in a village or a city or in an empty forest, if someone comes wanting to challenge them with hard questions, the gods day and night will protect them for the sake of the Dharma. They'll make everyone who hears rejoice.
Normal: Why? Because this sutra is protected by the spiritual power of all Buddhas—past, future, and present.
Normal: Mañjuśrī, this Lotus Sutra—in countless lands you can't even hear its name, much less see it, hold it, read it, or recite it!"
Heading 2: THE PARABLE OF THE KING'S CROWN JEWEL
Normal: "Mañjuśrī, let me tell you a story so you understand what I'm saying:
Normal: Imagine a powerful wheel-turning king—a king who rules with righteousness. He wants to bring all the nations under his rule using his authority. But some small kings won't submit to his command.
Normal: So this wheel-turning king raises up an army and goes to war against them. When he sees his soldiers fighting with courage, accomplishing difficult things, he's filled with joy. According to what they've accomplished, he gives rewards.
Normal: He gives them fields and houses, villages and cities. He gives them fine clothes and beautiful ornaments. He gives them all kinds of treasures—gold and silver, lapis lazuli, mother-of-pearl, agate, coral and amber. He gives them elephants and horses and carriages, slaves and servants, common people to work their lands.
Normal: But there's one thing he doesn't give: the bright jewel in his crown—the pearl on top of his head. Why? Because only the king has this one jewel, this unique treasure at the very crown of his head. If he gave it away, all his retinue would be shocked and amazed.
Normal: Well, Mañjuśrī, the Tathāgata is like this. Through the power of meditation and wisdom, he gained the territory of the Dharma. He rules over the three realms. But the demon kings wouldn't submit.
Normal: So the Tathāgata's worthy sages—his spiritual warriors—fought against those demons. When they showed great accomplishment, the Tathāgata's heart was filled with joy.
Normal: In the assembly of the four groups, he taught all kinds of sutras to make their hearts rejoice. He gave them the treasures of meditation and liberation, of undefiled roots and powers, of various dharmas. He also gave them the city of nirvāṇa, telling them they'd reached extinction. He guided their hearts and made them all rejoice.
Normal: But he didn't teach them this Lotus Sutra. Not yet.
Normal: Mañjuśrī, it's like when that wheel-turning king saw soldiers accomplish great things—things hard to believe—he was so joyful that he finally gave them that jewel that's hard to believe in, that pearl he kept so long in his crown, that treasure he never casually gave to anyone. Now he gives it.
Normal: The Tathāgata is like this. In the three realms he's the great Dharma king. With teachings he educates all beings. He sees his army of sages fighting against the five-aggregate demon, the affliction demon, and the death demon. He sees them accomplish great merit—destroying the three poisons, escaping the three realms, breaking through the demon's net.
Normal: At that time the Tathāgata is greatly joyful.
Normal: This Lotus Sutra can lead beings to complete wisdom. All the world finds it hard to believe—full of hatred for it, hard to trust. This is what he never taught before. But now he teaches it.
Normal: Mañjuśrī, this Lotus Sutra is the first teaching among all the Tathāgatas' teachings. Among all teachings, it's the most profound. At the very end he bestows it, just like that powerful king finally giving up that bright pearl he protected so long.
Normal: Mañjuśrī, this Lotus Sutra is the secret treasury of all Buddhas and Tathāgatas. Among all sutras, it stands at the very top. Through the long night I've guarded it, never carelessly teaching it. But now today I give it to you all and expound it fully."

Normal: END OF CHAPTER FOURTEEN: HOW TO KEEP YOUR SOUL CLEAN WHEN THE WORLD'S GONE WRONG
Heading 2: INTERPRETATION NOTES:
Normal: This chapter is survival wisdom for spiritual teachers in corrupt times. The Buddha ain't talking theory here—he's giving practical instructions for how to keep your soul clean when the world's gone wrong.
Normal: The four practices are like concentric circles of protection:
Normal: Your inner ground (patience, non-grasping, seeing clearly)
Normal: Your outer associations (who you don't run with, what you don't do)
Normal: Your speech and heart (how you talk, what you hold inside)
Normal: Your ultimate compassion (even for those who reject you)
Normal: The crown jewel parable is central: The Lotus Sutra is what the Buddha held back until his spiritual warriors had proven themselves, until they'd fought through their own demons and poisons. It's the final gift, the supreme teaching, given only when folks are ready.
Normal: And the beautiful dreams at the end—that's confirmation. That's how you know you're on the right path. When you hold this teaching right, it holds you back. You walk protected. Your dreams become prophecies. Even sleep becomes teaching.
Normal: This is practical mysticism. This is how you teach the highest truth in the lowest times without becoming what you're fighting against.
Heading 1: CHAPTER FIFTEEN: WHEN THE UNDERGROUND ARMY ROSE UP
Normal: A Blues Interpretation from the Classical Chinese
Heading 2: THE OFFER THAT GOT TURNED DOWN
Normal: Now at that time, all them bodhisattvas from other worlds—countless worlds beyond counting, more than eight Ganges rivers full of sand—they stood up in that great gathering. They pressed their palms together, bowed down low, and said to the Buddha:
Normal: "World-Honored One, if you let us—when you gone from this world, after you passed on—we will stay right here in this Śākyamuni realm, this troubled world called Sahā. We will work hard, we will stay diligent, we will protect this sutra, read it, recite it, write it down, make offerings to it. We will teach it far and wide in this land here."
Normal: But then the Buddha, he told all them bodhisattvas—all them great beings from other worlds:
Normal: "Stop. Stop right there, good sons. You don't need to protect this sutra. You don't need to worry yourselves about it.
Normal: Why's that?
Normal: Because my Śākyamuni world—this world right here—it already got 60,000 times the sands of the Ganges River worth of great bodhisattvas. And every single one of them bodhisattvas, they each got their own retinue—60,000 Ganges-sands worth of followers each.
Normal: And these people—all these beings right here—they able to protect this sutra after I'm gone. They can hold it, read it, recite it, teach it wide."
Heading 2: THE EARTH SPLITS WIDE OPEN
Normal: Now when the Buddha spoke them words, the whole Śākyamuni world—all three thousand great thousand realms of it—the ground started shaking and trembling and splitting apart.
Normal: And out from them cracks, out from underneath, there came bursting forth countless thousands, tens of thousands, millions, billions of bodhisattvas—great bodhisattvas, mighty bodhisattvas—all at the same time, all rising up together like a flood, like a army, like the morning breaking.
Normal: And these bodhisattvas, every one of them had bodies of gold—golden like the sunrise, golden like pure truth. They all had the thirty-two marks, they all shining with boundless light, they all radiant beyond measure.
Normal: And all along, all this time before now, they'd been living right underneath this Śākyamuni world—down below in the empty space beneath this realm—just dwelling there, waiting there, ready there.
Normal: These bodhisattvas, they heard Śākyamuni Buddha's voice when he spoke, and they came up from below. They answered the call.
Heading 2: THE VAST NUMBERS THAT NOBODY CAN COUNT
Normal: Now every one of these bodhisattvas, they was leaders—great leaders, mighty leaders—leading the masses, guiding the multitudes.
Normal: And each one was bringing their own followers with them:
Normal: Some had retinues of 60,000 Ganges-sands worth,
Normal: Some had 50,000 Ganges-sands,
Normal: Some 40,000, some 30,000, some 20,000, some 10,000 Ganges-sands of followers.
Normal: And then there was those with one Ganges-sand worth,
Normal: Or half a Ganges-sand,
Normal: Or a quarter, or one-eighth,
Normal: Or down to a thousand million billion nayutas fraction of a Ganges-sand.
Normal: And some had a thousand million billion nayutas of disciples,
Normal: Some had a hundred million or ten million,
Normal: Some had a million, hundred thousand, down to ten thousand.
Normal: Some had a thousand, a hundred, down to ten.
Normal: Some brought five disciples, some four, some three, some two, some just one.
Normal: And some came alone—single and solitary, loving the quiet path, walking the remote road by themselves.
Normal: On and on like this—countless, boundless, beyond all calculation, beyond all comparison, beyond all arithmetic, beyond what numbers can measure or words can tell.
Heading 2: THE GREAT ASSEMBLY AND THE LONG PRAISE
Normal: When all these bodhisattvas came up from the earth, they each went to the jeweled stupa in the sky—to where Abundant Treasures Tathāgata and Śākyamuni Buddha was sitting together.
Normal: When they got there, they bowed down before both World-Honored Ones, touched their heads to the feet of both Buddhas. They went to all the Buddha-copies sitting under the jeweled trees on lion thrones throughout the realms, and they bowed before each one too.
Normal: They circled them three times to the right, then stood with palms pressed together in deep respect. And they praised the Buddhas with all manner of bodhisattva praise-forms—praising and honoring, then standing to one side, gazing up joyfully at the two World-Honored Ones.
Normal: Now these great bodhisattvas, from the time they first burst forth from the earth, they was praising the Buddhas with all kinds of bodhisattva praise-forms. And this praising—this honoring and celebrating—it went on for FIFTY SMALL KALPAS. Fifty ages. Fifty long stretches of time.
Normal: And during all this time, Śākyamuni Buddha sat there silent. And all the four assemblies—they was silent too. Fifty small kalpas they was silent.
Normal: But because of the Buddha's spiritual power, he made it seem to that great assembly like only half a day had passed. Half a day! Time got bent, time got folded, time got compressed by the Buddha's power.
Normal: And also because of the Buddha's spiritual power, the four assemblies could see all them bodhisattvas filling up the empty space of countless hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of realms—filling it all up, everywhere you looked.
Heading 2: THE FOUR GREAT LEADERS STEP FORWARD
Normal: Now among all that vast bodhisattva multitude, there was four leaders—four chief guides, four head teachers:
Normal: The first was named SUPERIOR PRACTICE (上行 - Viśiṣṭhacāritra),
Normal: The second was named BOUNDLESS PRACTICE (無邊行 - Anantacāritra),
Normal: The third was named PURE PRACTICE (淨行 - Viśuddhacāritra),
Normal: The fourth was named WELL-ESTABLISHED PRACTICE (安立行 - Supratiṣṭhitacāritra).
Normal: These four bodhisattvas—they was the highest leaders, the chief guides among all that crowd.
Normal: They came forward in front of the great assembly. They pressed their palms together, gazed at Śākyamuni Buddha, and asked respectfully:
Normal: "World-Honored One, are you well? Do you have few sicknesses? Few troubles? Are you dwelling in peace and ease? Are the beings you teaching—are they easy to teach? Are they receiving instruction without resistance? We hope you not worn out, not exhausted, not burdened down by the work."
Heading 2: THE FOUR LEADERS SPEAK IN VERSE
Normal: Is the World-Honored One dwelling in peace,
Normal: with few sicknesses, few troubles?
Normal: Teaching all these living beings—
Normal: do you find yourself growing weary?
Normal: And are these living beings
Normal: easy to teach, easy to reach?
Normal: We hope they don't make the World-Honored One
Normal: tired, worn down, heavy-burdened.
Heading 2: THE BUDDHA SAYS: "IT AIN'T BEEN HARD"
Normal: Then the World-Honored One, there in the midst of that vast bodhisattva assembly, he said:
Normal: "Yes, yes, good sons. The Tathāgata is dwelling in peace. I got few sicknesses, few troubles. And these living beings—they easy to teach. There ain't been no weariness, no fatigue.
Normal: Why's that?
Normal: Because these living beings, life after life, world after world, age after age, they been receiving my teaching all along. And also in ages past, under previous Buddhas, they showed respect and reverence, and they planted all kinds of good roots.
Normal: So when these beings first saw my body, when they first heard what I was saying, they believed right away. They received it and entered into the Tathāgata's wisdom—just like that.
Normal: Now there's some exceptions—those who studied the small vehicle before, the lesser teachings. But even those people, I'm making sure they hear this sutra now, so they can enter into the Buddha's wisdom too."
Heading 2: THE GREAT BODHISATTVAS REJOICE
Normal: Then at that time, all them great bodhisattvas spoke in verse, saying:
Normal: Excellent! Excellent!
Normal: Great Hero, World-Honored One,
Normal: All these living beings—
Normal: they easy to teach, easy to guide.
Normal: They able to ask the Buddhas
Normal: about deep wisdom, profound truth.
Normal: Hearing it, they believe and practice—
Normal: and we rejoice along with them!
Heading 2: THE BUDDHA PRAISES HIS STUDENTS
Normal: Then the World-Honored One praised them chief bodhisattvas, saying:
Normal: "Excellent! Excellent, good sons! You able to rejoice along with the Tathāgata—able to be glad in the Tathāgata's work. That's good, that's real good."
Heading 2: MAITREYA'S MIND STARTS SPINNING
Normal: Now at that time, Maitreya Bodhisattva and 8,000 Ganges-sands worth of other bodhisattvas—they all had this thought arise in their minds:
Normal: "All this time up till now—from way back, from the beginning—we never seen, never heard tell of such a vast assembly of great bodhisattvas bursting up from the earth like this, standing before the World-Honored One, palms pressed together, making offerings, asking after the Tathāgata.
Normal: Where did they come from? What is this?"

Heading 2: THE BUDDHAS IN ALL DIRECTIONS WONDER TOO
Normal: Then at that time, all them emanation-bodies of Śākyamuni Buddha—all them Buddha-copies who came from countless thousands of millions of billions of other lands, sitting on lion thrones under jeweled trees throughout the eight directions—each one of their attendants saw this great assembly of bodhisattvas bursting up from the earth in the four directions of the three thousand great thousand worlds, rising up into empty space.

Heading 2: THE SHOCKING TRUTH BEGINS TO EMERGE
Normal: Then after the World-Honored One finished speaking this verse, he told Maitreya Bodhisattva:
Normal: "I'm now declaring to all of you in this great assembly—
Normal: Ajita! These great bodhisattvas, these innumerable, uncountable, inconceivable numbers of great beings bursting up from the earth that you never seen before—
Normal: After I attained supreme perfect enlightenment here in this Śākyamuni world, I taught and guided these bodhisattvas. I tamed their minds, caused them to give rise to the intention for the Way.
Normal: All these bodhisattvas have been dwelling right here—underneath this Śākyamuni world, in the empty space below this realm.
Normal: As for the sutras and scriptures, they read them, recite them, understand them thoroughly. They think about them, analyze them, contemplate them correctly and remember them right.
Normal: Ajita, these good sons—they don't love being in crowds with a lot of talking. They always love quiet places where they can practice vigorously without ever resting.
Normal: They don't depend on human or heavenly realms for their dwelling.
Normal: They always love deep wisdom without obstacles or hindrances. And they always love the Dharma of all Buddhas. With single mind and vigorous effort, they seeking supreme wisdom without cease."

Heading 2: MAITREYA'S MIND CAN'T TAKE IT: THE IMPOSSIBLE MATH
Normal: Now at that time, Maitreya Bodhisattva and countless other bodhisattvas—their minds filled up with doubt. They bewildered, amazed, never experienced nothing like this before.
Normal: And they thought:
Normal: "How could the World-Honored One in such a short time teach and guide such countless, boundless, innumerable great bodhisattvas and cause them to dwell in supreme perfect enlightenment?"
Normal: So Maitreya said directly to the Buddha:
Normal: "World-Honored One, when the Tathāgata was still a prince, he left the palace of the Śākya clan. He went not far from the city of Gayā, sat at the place of enlightenment, and attained supreme perfect enlightenment.
Normal: From that time till now, it's only been a little more than forty years.
Normal: World-Honored One, how could you in this short time accomplish such a great Buddha-work? How could you, with the Buddha's power and the Buddha's merit, teach and guide such countless great bodhisattvas to the point where they gonna attain supreme perfect enlightenment?
Heading 2: THE STORY NOBODY CAN BELIEVE
Normal: "World-Honored One, this great assembly of bodhisattvas—even if someone spent a thousand million billion kalpas trying to count them, they couldn't finish, couldn't reach the end.
Normal: These beings—from the distant, remote past—they been planting good roots under countless, boundless Buddhas. They done perfected the bodhisattva way. They always been practicing the pure conduct.
Normal: World-Honored One, such a thing as this—the world finds it hard to believe.
Normal: It's like if there was a man with beautiful features and black hair, only twenty-five years old, and he pointed at a hundred-year-old man and said, 'This is my son.' And the hundred-year-old man also pointed at the young one and said, 'This is my father who gave birth to me and raised me.'
Normal: Now that would be hard to believe, wouldn't it?"
Heading 2: THE DEPTH OF THE PROBLEM
Normal: "It's the same with the Buddha. You only attained the Way a short while ago—that's the truth of it.
Normal: But this great assembly of bodhisattvas—they already been practicing for countless thousands of millions of billions of kalpas for the sake of the Buddha-way. They been practicing vigorously, diligently.
Normal: They skilled at entering, leaving, and dwelling in countless hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of samādhis—deep meditations beyond measure. They obtained great spiritual powers. For a long time they been practicing pure conduct.
Normal: They able to practice good dharmas in proper sequence, step by step. They skillful at questions and answers. They treasures among human beings. They extremely rare in all the worlds.
Normal: And yet today the World-Honored One is saying that when you first attained the Buddha-way, you caused them to first give rise to the aspiration, then taught and guided them, directing them toward supreme perfect enlightenment.
Normal: World-Honored One, you ain't been Buddha for long—and yet you been able to accomplish this great work of merit!
Normal: Now we do believe in the Buddha. We believe whatever the Buddha says is appropriate to the situation. We know the Buddha's words never empty or false. We know the Buddha's knowledge penetrates everything thoroughly.
Normal: But still—
Normal: Those bodhisattvas who newly given rise to intention, who just starting out—if they hear these words after the Buddha passes away, they might not believe and accept it. And that might cause them to commit the sin of slandering the Dharma, breaking faith with the teaching.
Normal: So please, World-Honored One, explain this for us. Remove our doubts. And also for the good sons and daughters of future ages—when they hear about this matter, let them not have doubts either."
