Normal: To all them people far and wide.
Normal: All them people who was clinging to doctrines,
Normal: Every one of them received teaching
Normal: From this Bodhisattva,
Normal: Was brought to accomplishment,
Normal: Was caused to dwell in the Buddha-way.
Normal: When Never Looked Down's life ended,
Normal: He met countless Buddhas.
Normal: Because he taught this sutra,
Normal: He gained immeasurable blessings,
Normal: Gradually perfected his merit,
Normal: And quickly accomplished the Buddha-way.
Normal: That Never Looked Down back then -
Normal: That was my own self.
Normal: Them four kinds of people at that time,
Normal: The ones who was clinging to doctrines,
Normal: Who heard Never Looked Down say
Normal: "You gonna become a Buddha" -
Normal: Because of that cause and condition,
Normal: They met countless Buddhas.
Normal: These Bodhisattvas in this assembly,
Normal: Five hundred of them,
Normal: And also them four kinds -
Normal: Monks and nuns, believing laymen and laywomen,
Normal: The ones now standing before me
Normal: Listening to the Dharma - that's who they are.
Normal: In my former lives,
Normal: I urged all these people
Normal: To listen and receive this sutra,
Normal: This foremost teaching among teachings.
Normal: I opened it up and showed them,
Normal: I taught them the way,
Normal: I caused them to dwell in nirvāṇa.
Normal: Life after life they received and held
Normal: A sutra like this one.
Normal: For billions and billions of myriads of ages,
Normal: So many you can't even think about it,
Normal: Only then do you get to hear
Normal: This Lotus Sutra.
Normal: For billions and billions of myriads of ages,
Normal: So many you can't even think about it,
Normal: The Buddhas, the World-Honored Ones,
Normal: Only once in a while teach this sutra.
Normal: Therefore, you practitioners,
Normal: After the Buddha has passed into extinction,
Normal: When you hear a sutra like this,
Normal: Don't let doubt arise in your hearts.
Normal: You should with single mind
Normal: Teach this sutra far and wide.
Normal: Life after life you'll meet Buddhas,
Normal: And quickly accomplish the Buddha-way.
Normal: END OF CHAPTER TWENTY: THE BODHISATTVA WHO NEVER LOOKED DOWN
Heading 2: INTERPRETATION NOTES:
Normal: This chapter is pure blues architecture. The Never Looked Down Bodhisattva is the archetypal blues hero - maintaining dignity, faith, and prophetic voice in the face of relentless persecution. The repetitive structure mirrors both the repetition in blues music and the call-and-response tradition.
Normal: The interpretation uses vernacular English to convey deep theological concepts. For example, "You gonna become a Buddha" is not just a prediction but a prophetic declaration of an ontological truth that exists independent of current appearances. This resonates with the African American prophetic tradition where "gonna" is used to declare certain futures against present evidence.
Normal: The story of Never Looked Down teaches that you can remove yourself from immediate danger (running from the stones) while still maintaining your prophetic witness (shouting from a distance). It's a survival strategy and spiritual practice combined.
Normal: The ultimate revelation is that the persecutors, after suffering the consequences of their actions, are met again by Never Looked Down and finally receive the teaching. This is not revenge, but transformation—the ultimate blues vision of justice where even the oppressor is liberated.
Heading 1: CHAPTER TWENTY-ONE: WHEN THE LORD SHOWED HIS HAND
Normal: A Blues Interpretation from the Classical Chinese
Heading 2: PART ONE: THE VOW TO WITNESS
Normal: Now listen here—at that time, all them Bodhisattvas what come up from the earth, countless as dust motes in a thousand worlds, they all standing there before the Buddha, hands pressed together, gazing up at that holy face, and they speaking out their hearts:
Normal: "World-Honored One, after you done gone on from this world, wherever your presence still abiding—in all them lands where your manifested bodies been teaching, in every place where you entered into rest—we gonna spread this sutra far and wide.
Normal: Why we saying this? Because we ourselves want to get hold of this true and pure Great Law, want to keep it, read it, recite it, explain it, write it down, and make offerings to it."
Heading 2: PART TWO: THE GREAT REVEALING
Normal: Now at that time the World-Honored One, right there before Mañjuśrī and all them countless hundreds of thousands of myriads of millions of Bodhisattvas what been dwelling in this Saha world from way back, and before all the monks and nuns, the laymen and laywomen, the devas and dragons and yakshas and gandharvas and asuras and garudas and kinnaras and mahoragas, before humans and non-humans alike—before EVERY LIVING THING THAT EVER WAS—the Buddha showed forth his great supernatural power.
Normal: And what he do?
Normal: He put out his broad long tongue, and it reached straight up to the Brahma heaven.
Normal: From every pore of his body he released immeasurable, numberless colored lights, and they shone everywhere throughout the ten directions.
Normal: And all them other Buddhas sitting on lion thrones under jeweled trees, they did the same thing—put out they broad long tongues and released immeasurable light.
Normal: When Śākyamuni Buddha and all them Buddhas under the jeweled trees was showing forth they supernatural power, it lasted for a hundred thousand years.
Normal: Then they drew back they tongue-signs.
Normal: And then—oh, then!—they coughed once, ALL TOGETHER, and snapped they fingers, ALL AT THE SAME TIME.
Normal: And them two sounds—that cough and that finger-snap—they traveled to all the Buddha-worlds in the ten directions.
Normal: And the earth, she shook six ways.
Heading 2: PART THREE: THE UNIVERSAL WITNESS
Normal: Now all the living beings in them worlds—the devas and dragons and yakshas and gandharvas and asuras and garudas and kinnaras and mahoragas, humans and non-humans—through the Buddha's supernatural power, they ALL SAW this Saha world.
Normal: They saw immeasurable, boundless hundreds of thousands of myriads of millions of Buddhas sitting on lion thrones under jeweled trees.
Normal: They saw Śākyamuni Buddha sitting together with Many Treasures Tathāgata on the lion throne inside that jeweled stupa.
Normal: They saw immeasurable, boundless hundreds of thousands of myriads of millions of Bodhisattvas and the fourfold assembly respectfully surrounding Śākyamuni Buddha.
Normal: When they seen all this, they was filled with great joy—they got something they never had before!
Heading 2: PART FOUR: THE CALL AND THE RESPONSE
Normal: Right then and there, the devas in empty space, they raised up they voices high and made this proclamation:
Normal: "Beyond these immeasurable, boundless hundreds of thousands of myriads of millions of asamkhyeya worlds, there's a land called Saha. In that land there's a Buddha called Śākyamuni. Right now he teaching the great vehicle sutra to the Bodhisattvas—it called the Wonderful Dharma Lotus Flower, the teaching for Bodhisattvas, the one the Buddha guards and keeps in mind.
Normal: Y'all should rejoice from the bottom of your hearts! You should bow down and make offerings to Śākyamuni Buddha!"
Normal: When all them beings heard that voice from empty space, they pressed they palms together, turned toward the Saha world, and said:
Normal: "Glory to Śākyamuni Buddha! Glory to Śākyamuni Buddha!"
Normal: They took all kinds of flowers and incense and necklaces, banners and canopies, jewels and precious ornaments for adorning the body, and they scattered them from afar toward the Saha world.
Normal: All them scattered things coming from the ten directions, they gathered like clouds, transformed into jeweled canopies, and spread out covering all the Buddhas there.
Normal: And in that time, the worlds of the ten directions was completely open and unobstructed, like one Buddha land.
Heading 2: PART FIVE: THE ENTRUSTMENT
Normal: At that time the Buddha told Superior Practices and all them other Bodhisattvas:
Normal: "The supernatural powers of the Buddhas—they just like this: immeasurable, boundless, inconceivable. Even if I was to use these supernatural powers for immeasurable, boundless hundreds of thousands of myriads of millions of asamkhyeya kalpas, talking about the merit and virtue of this sutra for the sake of entrusting it to y'all, I still couldn't finish telling it.
Normal: Let me sum it up for you:
Normal: All the Dharmas the Tathāgata possesses,
Normal: All the sovereign supernatural powers of the Tathāgata,
Normal: All the storehouse of profound essentials of the Tathāgata,
Normal: All the most deep matters of the Tathāgata—
Normal: ALL OF IT is proclaimed and revealed and demonstrated in this sutra.
Normal: Therefore, after the Tathāgata done passed on into extinction, y'all should single-mindedly receive and keep, read and recite, explain and expound, transcribe and practice according to what it says.
Normal: In whatever land you find yourself, if someone receives and keeps, reads and recites, explains and expounds, transcribes and practices according to what this sutra says—or if there's a place where a sutra scroll dwells, whether in a garden, or in a grove, or under a tree, or in a monk's dwelling, or in a white-clothed person's house, or in a hall or palace, or in a mountain valley or wilderness—in that place you should build a stupa and make offerings.
Normal: Why is that? You should know: THAT PLACE IS THE SITE OF ENLIGHTENMENT.
Normal: The Buddhas attained anuttara-samyak-sambodhi at that place.
Normal: The Buddhas turned the Dharma wheel at that place.
Normal: The Buddhas entered nirvāṇa at that place."
Heading 2: PART SIX: THE SUTRA IN VERSE
Normal: The Buddhas, saviors of the world,
Normal: Dwelling in great supernatural penetrations,
Normal: In order to gladden living beings,
Normal: Display immeasurable supernatural powers.
Normal: They tongues reaching to the Brahma heaven,
Normal: They bodies releasing numberless lights—
Normal: For them seeking the Buddha Way,
Normal: They manifest these rare occurrences.
Normal: The sound of the Buddhas coughing,
Normal: The sound of they fingers snapping,
Normal: Heard throughout the lands in ten directions,
Normal: The earth shaking six ways everywhere.
Normal: Because after the Buddha's extinction
Normal: Someone able to uphold this sutra,
Normal: All the Buddhas rejoicing,
Normal: Display immeasurable supernatural powers.
Normal: For the sake of entrusting this sutra,
Normal: Praising those who receive and keep it,
Normal: Even through immeasurable kalpas
Normal: They still can't come to the end of it.
Normal: The merit and virtue of such a person—
Normal: Boundless, without limit,
Normal: Like the empty space of ten directions,

Normal: Gonna make them rejoice as well.

Normal: The Buddhas attained sitting at the place of enlightenment—
Normal: One who able to uphold this sutra
Normal: Gonna get it before too long.
Normal: One who able to uphold this sutra—
Normal: When it come to the meaning of all dharmas,
Normal: The names and the words,
Normal: They gonna preach with inexhaustible joy,
Normal: Like wind in empty space
Normal: That ain't got no obstruction nowhere.
Normal: After the Tathāgata's extinction,
Normal: They gonna know the sutras the Buddha taught,
Normal: The causes and conditions and the sequence,
Normal: And teach them according to the true meaning,
Normal: Like the light of sun and moon
Normal: That removes all darkness—
Normal: This person walking through the world
Normal: Able to destroy the darkness of living beings,
Normal: Teaching immeasurable Bodhisattvas,
Normal: Finally causing them to dwell in the One Vehicle.
Normal: Therefore, if you got wisdom,
Normal: Hearing these benefits and merits,
Normal: After my extinction
Normal: You should receive and uphold this sutra.
Normal: Such a person, on the Buddha Way,
Normal: Decidedly ain't got no doubt.
Normal: END OF CHAPTER TWENTY-ONE: WHEN THE LORD SHOWED HIS HAND
Heading 2: INTERPRETATION NOTES:
Normal: This chapter operates at the highest register in the entire Lotus Sutra—this is the moment when the Buddha "shows his hand," reveals the full scope of his power, and the entire universe bears witness. The challenge in a blues/gospel interpretation is to maintain both the vernacular authenticity AND the sense of cosmic scale.
Normal: The chapter is built on a call-and-response structure. The Buddha displays supernatural powers (the call), and all of creation responds with witness and praise. This is the ultimate revival meeting, where the congregation is the entire cosmos.
Normal: The Buddha's supernatural display here is not arbitrary showing-off—it's maximum communication. He's using every available channel to broadcast the truth: visual (tongue extending, light radiating), auditory (coughing, finger-snapping), and kinesthetic (earth shaking). This is multimedia theophany, truth that overflows every boundary.
Normal: The teaching that any place where the sutra dwells becomes a holy site—"THAT PLACE IS THE SITE OF ENLIGHTENMENT"—is a radical democratization of sacred space. The sacred isn't far away; it's right here, right now, wherever the Word is present.
Normal: The verse section makes an extraordinary claim: "One who able to uphold this sutra, / That person already seen me." To hold the sutra is to see the Buddha. The teaching and the teacher are not separate. This is the Lotus Sutra's core soteriology in a nutshell: to encounter the teaching is to encounter the teacher.

Normal: I'm entrusting it to you.

Normal: Spread it out with one mind,
Normal: Make it grow far and wide."

Normal: END OF CHAPTER TWENTY-TWO: THE PASSING ON
Heading 2: INTERPRETATION NOTES:
Normal: This chapter contains the most physically intimate moment in the entire Lotus Sutra. After twenty-one chapters of cosmic visions, parables, prophecies, and supernatural displays, we arrive at a simple human gesture: the Buddha rises from his seat and puts his hand on people's heads. Three times.
Normal: This is transmission through touch. Not through doctrine, not through vision, but through the laying on of hands—a gesture that runs deep in both Buddhist and Christian ritual practice. When the Buddha's hand comes down on those Bodhisattvas' heads, something passes. Not just information, but authorization. Not just teaching, but succession. Not just wisdom, but responsibility.
Normal: The threefold repetition is crucial. In both Buddhist and gospel traditions, three is the number of confirmation. When the Buddha lays his hand on their heads three times and speaks the commission three times, he's making it stick. He's sealing it in the body, in the memory, in the muscle.
Normal: The practical wisdom in this chapter is beautiful: "If they believe, teach them the Lotus. If they don't believe, teach them something else from the Buddha's deep teachings that they can receive." This is the opposite of rigidity. The point is liberation, not orthodoxy.
Normal: The chapter ends with a quiet dismissal. The cosmic drama is over. The work of transmission has been done. Now it's time to go home and get to work. The joy at the end is the joy of knowing what you're supposed to do.
Heading 1: CHAPTER TWENTY-THREE: MEDICINE KING BODHISATTVA - THE STORY OF HOW HE GAVE IT ALL
Normal: A Blues Interpretation from the Classical Chinese
Heading 2: PART ONE: THE QUESTION
Normal: Now at that time, Constellation King Flower Bodhisattva stood up and said to the Buddha:
Normal: "World-Honored One, how does Medicine King Bodhisattva walk through this suffering world of ours? World-Honored One, this Medicine King Bodhisattva—he done how many hundred thousand million billion impossible hard practices? Tell us, World-Honored One! We want to know a little bit about this story."
Normal: And all the gods in heaven, all the dragons, all the spirits, all the night-wanderers, the music-makers, the jealous fighting gods, the great bird-kings, the half-human singers, the great serpent spirits, the humans and the not-quite-humans, and all the bodhisattvas come from other Buddha-lands, and all the disciples gathered there—they all wanted to hear it too, and they were glad in their hearts.
Heading 2: PART TWO: THE OLD STORY - A LONG TIME BACK
Normal: Then the Buddha said to Constellation King Flower Bodhisattva:
Normal: "Listen now. A long time back—we talking about more ages past than there's grains of sand in the Ganges River—there was a Buddha called Sun Moon Pure Bright Virtue Thus Come One. He had all ten titles: Worthy of Offerings, Perfectly Enlightened in Right Knowledge, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Unsurpassed One, Tamer of Beings, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One.
Normal: "That Buddha, he had eighty billion great bodhisattvas—great beings, every one—and seventy-two times the sands of the Ganges River worth of great disciples who heard his teaching. That Buddha lived for forty-two thousand ages, and the bodhisattvas lived just as long.
Normal: "In that Buddha-land, there wasn't no women, no hell realms, no hungry ghost realms, no animal realms, no jealous fighting gods, none of that suffering business. The ground was flat and smooth as the palm of your hand, made of lapis lazuli stone—pure blue jewel-ground. Treasure trees stood everywhere for beauty, treasure canopies spread overhead, treasure flower banners hanging down. Treasure bottles and incense burners everywhere you looked, all through that land. Seven kinds of precious things made up the platforms, and every tree had its platform—each tree standing just one arrow-shot away from its platform.
Normal: "Under all them treasure trees, bodhisattvas and disciples sat in meditation. And up on all them treasure platforms, there was hundreds of billions of gods making heavenly music, singing praises to that Buddha, making offerings with their songs."
Heading 2: PART THREE: THE BODHISATTVA WHO EVERYBODY LOVED TO SEE
Normal: "Now at that time, that Buddha was preaching the Lotus Sutra to a bodhisattva called Gladly Seen by All Living Beings—yeah, 'Gladly Seen by All Living Beings,' that's his name—and to all the other bodhisattvas and disciples gathered there.
Normal: "This Gladly Seen by All Living Beings Bodhisattva, he loved to practice hard things. In the Dharma of Sun Moon Pure Bright Virtue Buddha, he practiced with intensity, walking meditation with his whole heart, seeking Buddhahood with everything he had. For twelve thousand full years he did this.
Normal: "Then he attained it—he got the samādhi called 'Manifestation of All Physical Forms.' Got that samādhi, and his heart was filled with great joy.
Normal: "He thought to himself: 'I got this Manifestation of All Physical Forms samādhi because I heard the Lotus Sutra. That's the power that did it. Now I got to make an offering to Sun Moon Pure Bright Virtue Buddha and to the Lotus Sutra.'
Normal: "Right then and there he entered that samādhi, and up in the empty sky he rained down mandarava flowers and great mandarava flowers. He rained down fine powdered hard black sandalwood—filled up the whole sky like clouds coming down. And he rained down sandalwood from the shore of the ocean—this sandalwood so precious that six ounces of it worth a whole world like ours—making offerings to that Buddha."
Heading 2: PART FOUR: WHEN THINGS AIN'T ENOUGH
Normal: "After making that offering, he came out of his samādhi and thought to himself:
Normal: 'Even though I made offerings to the Buddha with supernatural power, that ain't enough. I got to make an offering with my body.'
Normal: "So he started drinking fragrant oils—sandalwood oil, frankincense oil, turpentine oil, sweet-smelling oils, camphor oil, and all kinds of oils. He drank oils made from jasmine and all kinds of fragrant flower oils. He did this for one thousand two hundred years.
Normal: "After one thousand two hundred years, his whole body was saturated with fragrant oils. He rubbed more fragrant oils all over his body. Then, in front of Sun Moon Pure Bright Virtue Buddha, he wrapped himself in heavenly treasure cloth, poured more fragrant oils all over himself, and by the power of his supernatural vow, he set his own body on fire.
Normal: "The light from his burning body lit up eighty billion times the sands of the Ganges River worth of worlds.
Normal: "In all those worlds, the Buddhas all praised him at the same time, saying:
Normal: 'GOOD! GOOD! GOOD, good son! THIS is true intensity! THIS is what we call true Dharma-offering to the Thus Come One! Even if you make offerings with flowers, incense, necklaces, burning incense, powdered incense, anointing incense, heavenly silk banners and canopies, even sandalwood from the ocean shore—all kinds of things like that—can't match this. Even if you give away countries and cities, wives and children—can't match this. Good son, THIS is the first among all givings, the most honored, the most supreme among all offerings, because this is making Dharma-offerings to all the Thus Come Ones!'
Normal: "They said all that, then they fell silent.
Normal: "His body burned for one thousand two hundred years. After that time passed, his body was finally consumed."
Heading 2: PART FIVE: HE CAME BACK
Normal: "After Gladly Seen by All Living Beings Bodhisattva made that Dharma-offering, his life ended. But after his life ended, he was born again in the land of Sun Moon Pure Bright Virtue Buddha, in the house of Pure Virtue King. Sitting in full lotus position, he suddenly appeared—born by transformation.
Normal: "Right away he spoke a verse to his father:
Normal: Great King, you should know this now:
Normal: I walked in practice in that place,
Normal: And right away I got the samādhi
Normal: Called Manifestation of All Physical Forms.
Normal: I practiced with great intensity,
Normal: Gave up my beloved body,
Normal: Made offerings to the World-Honored One,
Normal: Seeking that supreme wisdom.
Normal: "After speaking that verse, he said to his father:
Normal: 'Sun Moon Pure Bright Virtue Buddha is still present right now. Before, I made offerings to that Buddha, and I gained the dhāraṇī for understanding the languages of all living beings. Plus, I heard this Lotus Sutra—eight hundred thousand million billion nayuta koṭi vimbaras and aśaṅkhyeya verses of it.
Normal: 'Great King, now I got to go back and make offerings to that Buddha again.'
Normal: "Soon as he said that, he sat himself on a seven-treasure platform and rose up into empty space—rose up high as seven tāla trees—and went to where that Buddha was. He bowed his head to the Buddha's feet, put his ten fingertips together, and praised the Buddha with a verse:
Normal: Your face is wonderfully strange and fine,
Normal: Your light shines through the ten directions,
Normal: I made offerings once before,
Normal: Now I come again to see you face to face.
Heading 2: PART SIX: THE BUDDHA'S PASSING - THE TRUST HANDED DOWN
Normal: "After Gladly Seen by All Living Beings Bodhisattva spoke that verse, he said to the Buddha:
Normal: 'World-Honored One, the World-Honored One is still present in the world!'
Normal: "Then Sun Moon Pure Bright Virtue Buddha said to Gladly Seen by All Living Beings Bodhisattva:
Normal: 'Good son, the time for my nirvāṇa has come. The time for extinction has arrived. You can prepare the bed and seat. Tonight, in the middle watch of the night, I will enter nirvāṇa.'
Normal: "And he charged Gladly Seen by All Living Beings Bodhisattva:
Normal: 'Good son, I entrust the Buddha-Dharma to you—to you and to all the bodhisattvas and great disciples, and also the Dharma of supreme perfect enlightenment. I also entrust to you the three-thousand great thousandfold seven-treasure world—all the treasure trees, treasure platforms, and the serving gods—I hand all of it over to you. After I pass into extinction, my relics—I entrust them to you too. You should distribute them widely, set up offerings far and wide. You should build several thousand stupas.'
Normal: "After Sun Moon Pure Bright Virtue Buddha charged Gladly Seen by All Living Beings Bodhisattva like that, in the last watch of the night, he entered nirvāṇa."
Heading 2: PART SEVEN: GRIEF AND THE FUNERAL FIRE
Normal: "When Gladly Seen by All Living Beings Bodhisattva saw the Buddha pass into extinction, he was struck with grief, brokenhearted, filled with longing for the Buddha.
Normal: "So he took sandalwood from the ocean shore and made a funeral pyre to honor the Buddha's body, and burned it.
Normal: "After the fire went out, he gathered the relics and made eighty-four thousand treasure urns. With those, he built eighty-four thousand stupas—high as three worlds, decorated with banners and flags, adorned with hanging canopies, with all kinds of treasure bells hanging down."
Heading 2: PART EIGHT: THE BURNING OF THE ARMS - WHEN THE BODY AIN'T COMPLETE NO MORE
Normal: "Then Gladly Seen by All Living Beings Bodhisattva thought to himself again:
Normal: 'Even though I made these offerings, my heart still ain't satisfied. I got to make more offerings to the relics.'
Normal: "So he said to all the bodhisattvas and great disciples and to the gods, dragons, night-wanderers, and all the great assembly:
Normal: 'Y'all should focus your hearts and minds. I'm about to make offerings now to the relics of Sun Moon Pure Bright Virtue Buddha.'
Normal: "After he said that, right there in front of those eighty-four thousand stupas, he burned his two arms—adorned with a hundred blessings, those arms were—and he burned them for seventy-two thousand years, making offerings.
Normal: "This caused countless people seeking to be disciples, and measureless uncountable people beyond measure, to bring forth the mind of supreme perfect enlightenment. And they all attained dwelling in the samādhi of Manifestation of All Physical Forms."
Heading 2: PART NINE: THE WITNESSES CRY OUT - THE BODY AIN'T WHOLE NO MORE
Normal: "Now when all them bodhisattvas, gods, humans, jealous fighting gods, and the rest saw he didn't have no arms, they were distressed and sorrowful and grief-struck, and they said:
Normal: 'This Gladly Seen by All Living Beings Bodhisattva is our teacher, the one who taught us and guided us. But now he burned his arms, and his body ain't complete no more!'
Heading 2: PART TEN: THE VOW - IF THIS IS REAL, LET IT RESTORE
Normal: "Right then, Gladly Seen by All Living Beings Bodhisattva stood there in the midst of that great assembly and made this vow:
Normal: 'I gave up both my arms. I WILL attain the Buddha's golden body. If that's real and not empty words, if that's true and not a lie, then let my two arms come back just like they were!'
Normal: "Soon as he made that vow, his arms naturally restored themselves—came back just like they were.
Normal: "This happened because of the deep merit, the thick virtue, the profound wisdom of that bodhisattva.
Normal: "Right at that time, the three-thousand great thousandfold world shook six ways. Heaven rained down treasure flowers. All the humans and gods experienced what they'd never experienced before."
Heading 2: PART ELEVEN: WHO HE IS NOW
Normal: The Buddha said to Constellation King Flower Bodhisattva:
Normal: "What do you think? Was Gladly Seen by All Living Beings Bodhisattva some other person? No sir! Right now, it's Medicine King Bodhisattva. He gave up his body and made offerings like that—countless hundreds of thousands of millions of billions beyond counting, that's how many times he gave.
Normal: "Constellation King Flower, if someone brings forth the mind seeking supreme perfect enlightenment, and they can burn even just one finger, or even just one toe, as an offering to a Buddha stupa—that's worth more than giving away countries, cities, wives, children, or even all the mountains, forests, rivers, and pools and precious treasures in a three-thousand great thousandfold world.
Normal: "And if someone fills up a three-thousand great thousandfold world with the seven treasures and makes offerings to the Buddha and to great bodhisattvas and to pratyekabuddhas and to arhats—the merit that person gets don't compare to someone who receives and keeps this Lotus Sutra, even just one four-line verse of it. THAT blessing is the greatest."
Heading 2: PART TWELVE: THE PRAISES - THIS SUTRA IS SUPREME
Normal: "Constellation King Flower, listen:

Normal: "And just like among earth mountains, black mountains, small iron-ring mountains, great iron-ring mountains, and the ten treasure mountains—among all mountains, Mount Sumeru is first—this Lotus Sutra is like that. Among all sutras, it's the highest.

Normal: "And just like the sun-child can drive out all darkness—this sutra is like that. It can break all the darkness of what ain't good.
Normal: "And just like among all the little kings, the Wheel-Turning Sacred King is first—this sutra is like that. Among all sutras, it's the most honored.
Normal: "And just like Indra is king among the thirty-three gods—this sutra is like that. It's king among all sutras.

Normal: "And just like among all ordinary people, the stream-enterer, the once-returner, the non-returner, the arhat, and the pratyekabuddha are first—this sutra is like that. Normal: "If someone can receive and keep this sutra, they're like that too—among all living beings, they're the very first.
Normal: "Among all disciples and pratyekabuddhas, the bodhisattvas are first. This sutra is like that—among all sutra-dharmas, it's the very first.
Normal: "Just like the Buddha is king of all dharmas, this sutra is like that—it's king among all sutras."
Heading 2: PART THIRTEEN: THE MEDICINE FOR EVERYTHING
Normal: "Constellation King Flower, this sutra can rescue all living beings. This sutra can cause all living beings to leave all suffering and distress. This sutra can greatly benefit all living beings, filling up their wishes.

Normal: "Like people finding a king.

Normal: "Like a torch driving out darkness.

Normal: "If a person gets to hear this Lotus Sutra—whether they copy it themselves or have someone else copy it—the merit they get, even if you measure it with the Buddha's wisdom, you can't find the edge of it.
Normal: "If someone copies this sutra scroll and makes offerings with flowers, incense, necklaces, burning incense, powdered incense, anointing incense, banners, canopies, robes, and all kinds of lamps—butter lamps, oil lamps, all kinds of fragrant oil lamps, jasmine oil lamps, sumana flower oil lamps, pāṭala oil lamps, vārṣika oil lamps, navamallikā oil lamps—making offerings like that, the merit they get is also measureless."
Heading 2: PART FOURTEEN: THE PROMISE TO WOMEN - YOU WON'T BE WOMEN NO MORE
Normal: "Constellation King Flower, if someone hears this Chapter on the Past Deeds of Medicine King Bodhisattva, they also get measureless, boundless merit.
Normal: "If a WOMAN hears this Chapter on the Past Deeds of Medicine King Bodhisattva and can receive and keep it—when she finishes this female body, she won't receive a female body ever again.
Normal: "If, after the Thus Come One's extinction, in the last five hundred years, if a woman hears this sutra and practices according to what it says—when this life ends, she'll go straight to the Land of Peace and Joy, to where Amitābha Buddha and the great bodhisattvas surround and dwell. She'll be born in a lotus flower, on a jeweled seat.
Normal: "She won't be troubled no more by greed and desire.

Normal: "Once she gets that tolerance, her eye-faculty will become pure. With that pure eye-faculty, she'll see seven hundred twenty billion nayuta times the sands of the Ganges River worth of Thus Come One Buddhas.
Heading 2: PART FIFTEEN: ALL THE BUDDHAS PRAISE HER FROM FAR AWAY
Normal: "At that time, all those Buddhas will praise her from far away, saying:

Normal: "Constellation King Flower, this bodhisattva accomplished the power of merit and wisdom just like that."
Heading 2: PART SIXTEEN: THE FRAGRANCE THEY CARRY

Normal: "That's why, Constellation King Flower, I'm entrusting this Chapter on the Past Deeds of Medicine King Bodhisattva to you. Don't let evil demons, demon people, gods, dragons, night-wanderers, or kumbhāṇḍa spirits get their chance at it."
Heading 2: PART SEVENTEEN: THIS SUTRA IS MEDICINE - DON'T GET OLD, DON'T DIE

Normal: "If a person has a disease and gets to hear this sutra, their disease will disappear and be gone. They won't get old. They won't die.
Heading 2: PART EIGHTEEN: WHAT TO DO WHEN YOU SEE SOMEONE KEEPING THIS SUTRA
Normal: "Constellation King Flower, if you see someone who receives and keeps this sutra, you should take blue lotus flowers, fill them with powdered incense, and scatter them over that person. After you scatter them, you should think like this:
Normal: 'This person before long—won't be long now—they gonna take the grass and sit down at the place of enlightenment. They gonna break all the demon armies. They gonna blow the Dharma conch. They gonna beat the great Dharma drum. They gonna ferry across all living beings from the ocean of old age, sickness, and death.'
Normal: "That's why—anyone seeking the Buddha Way, when they see someone receiving and keeping this sutra, they should bring forth a respectful mind just like that toward them."
Heading 2: PART NINETEEN: WHAT HAPPENED WHEN HE TOLD THIS STORY
Normal: When the Buddha told this Chapter on the Past Deeds of Medicine King Bodhisattva, eighty-four thousand bodhisattvas attained the dhāraṇī for understanding the languages of all living beings.
Normal: Many Treasures Thus Come One, there in his treasure stupa, praised Constellation King Flower Bodhisattva, saying:
Normal: "GOOD! GOOD! Constellation King Flower, you accomplished inconceivable merit. You were able to ask Śākyamuni Buddha about matters like this, benefiting measureless, all living beings."
Normal: END OF CHAPTER TWENTY-THREE: MEDICINE KING BODHISATTVA - THE STORY OF HOW HE GAVE IT ALL
Heading 2: INTERPRETATION NOTES:
Normal: This chapter contains some of the most extreme imagery in all of Buddhist literature: a bodhisattva who saturates his body with fragrant oils for 1,200 years, then sets himself on fire and burns for another 1,200 years. Later, he burns both his arms for 72,000 years.
Normal: In the Buddhist context, this represents
Normal: total self-offering
Normal: as the ultimate form of generosity (dāna-pāramitā). The burning body produces
Normal: light
Normal: that illuminates eighty billion worlds. This transforms the act from destruction into illumination. The bodhisattva becomes a lamp, a torch that lights up reality for countless beings. His sacrifice becomes revelation.
Normal: The most dramatic moment is when Medicine King, after burning his arms, makes a vow: "If it's true I will attain the Buddha's golden body, let my arms be restored." And they are. This is about the power of vow (praṇidhāna) and the indestructibility of the Dharma-body. What is given fully for the sake of truth is never truly lost.
Normal: The chapter also contains a radical promise of liberation for women, stating that any woman who hears and keeps this chapter will not be reborn in a female body. This challenges the patriarchal context of its time, suggesting that ultimate commitment to the Dharma transcends all social and physical limitations.
Normal: Finally, the theme of fragrance—saturating the body with it, emanating it—symbolizes virtue that arises naturally from practice. The practitioner doesn't just *make* offerings; they *become* an offering, their very presence a benefit to the world.

Normal: and all the difficult places—he can bring salvation.
Normal: Even in the inner palaces of kings,
Normal: he transforms into a woman's body to teach this sutra."
Heading 2: THE SCOPE OF THE WORK
Normal: "Flower Virtue, this Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva
Normal: can protect and save all living beings in the Saha world.
Normal: This Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva manifests and transforms like this,
Normal: END OF CHAPTER TWENTY-FOUR: WONDERFUL SOUND BODHISATTVA
Heading 2: INTERPRETATION NOTES:
Normal: This chapter is a pilgrimage story—a narrative about answering a call, making a sacred journey, and returning home transformed and transformative. It's structured like a classic hero's journey, but the hero here is already enlightened. He ain't going to learn something; he's going to witness something and to serve.
Normal: The Warning About Looking Down:
Normal: The Buddha's warning to Wonderful Sound not to look down on the "rough" Saha world is a crucial teaching on respect and not confusing appearance with essence. The Saha world may look small and troubled, but it's where the work is, where beings need saving.
Normal: Traveling Without Moving:
Normal: Wonderful Sound doesn't physically leave his seat but enters samādhi, and by that power, he appears at Vulture Peak. This is a teaching on the nature of spiritual travel and the power of a concentrated mind to transcend physical distance.
Normal: The Power to Manifest in All Forms:
Normal: The heart of this chapter is the list of forms that Wonderful Sound can take to teach the Dharma. He becomes whatever form people need to see in order to hear the teaching. This is radical adaptability in the service of truth, the ultimate expression of skillful means. The samādhi that allows this is called "Manifesting All Bodies."
Normal: The chapter follows the classic structure of a spiritual journey: The call is heard, the journey is made in faith, respect is paid, the teaching is received and given, and the pilgrim returns to share the fruits of the journey, transforming others in the process.

Heading 2: THE QUESTION
Normal: Right then, the Bodhisattva named Inexhaustible Intention - he rose up from his seat, bared his right shoulder in that ancient way of showing respect, pressed his palms together before the Buddha, and said:
Normal: "World-Honored One, I got to ask you something. This Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara - Observer of the World's Sounds - why she called that? What's the reason, what's the cause behind that name?"
Normal: And the Buddha told Inexhaustible Intention:
Normal: "Good friend, listen now. She gonna observe the very sound of their crying. And every single one gonna find liberation, gonna get free.

Heading 2: THE TESTIMONY
Normal: Right then, Earth-Holding Bodhisattva stood up from his seat,
Normal: Came forward and said to the Buddha:
Normal: "World-Honored One, if beings hear this chapter about Avalokiteśvara -
Normal: About her sovereign works,

Heading 2: INTERPRETATION NOTES:
Normal: For sixteen hundred years, this chapter has been the most beloved, most memorized, most chanted part of the entire Lotus Sutra across East Asia. This ain't abstract philosophy - this is practical theology for people who are drowning, people in chains, people facing the fire.
Normal: The structure is pure call-and-response. The litany of dangers and deliverances builds a rhythm of faith. The core teaching is that Avalokiteśvara, the Observer of the World's Sounds, doesn't have one fixed form. She appears as whatever you need: a Buddha, a priest, a woman, a child, even a demon-king. This is the Incarnation principle taken universal. The Word becomes flesh—not just once, but everywhere, all the time, in whatever flesh is needed.
Normal: The chapter's power lies in its promise of immediate response. She doesn't judge; she HEARS and RESPONDS. In blues terms: she hears the blue note in your voice, the bent note that means pain, and she answers it. This is the gospel promise of a God who HEARS and ANSWERS. Not a distant philosophical principle, but an intimate responding presence.
Heading 1: CHAPTER TWENTY-SIX: THE PROTECTION SONGS
Normal: A Blues Interpretation from the Classical Chinese
Heading 2: WHEN MEDICINE KING STEPS UP
Normal: Now right then, Medicine King Bodhisattva—you remember him, the one who burned his own body to show his devotion—he stood up from his seat, put his robe over one shoulder the way you do when you're about to say something serious, pressed his palms together, and spoke to the Buddha:
Normal: "World-Honored One, listen now. If there's a good man or a good woman—I'm talking about anybody who's got the heart—if they can hold on to this Lotus teaching, if they can read it and speak it and know it through and through, if they can write it down with their own hand, tell me: How much blessing does that soul receive?"
Normal: And the Buddha said to Medicine King: "Let me ask you something first. If there was a good man or a good woman, and they made offerings to eight hundred myriads of millions of nayutas of Buddhas—as many Buddhas as there are grains of sand in the Ganges River—what you think? Would their blessing be great, or would it be small?"
Normal: "It would be great, World-Honored One. Lord, it would be mighty great."
Normal: The Buddha said: "Now let me tell you something. If a good man or a good woman can hold on to even one four-line verse of this teaching—just four lines!—if they can read it and speak it and understand what it means, if they can practice what it says, their merit is GREATER THAN THAT. You hear what I'm saying? Greater than all that other merit combined."
Normal: Right then Medicine King said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, I'm about to give a protection song—a dhāraṇī—to those who teach this Dharma. I'm gonna stand guard over them."
Normal: And he spoke the powerful words:
Normal: ANYE MANYE MANE MAMANE CHITE CHARITE
Normal: SHAME SHAMITARE SHANTE MUKTE MUKTAME
Normal: SAME AVISAME SAMASAME JAYE KSHAYE
Normal: AKSHINE SHANTE SHAME DHĀRAṆĪ

Normal: UKKULE MUKKULE ARADE PARADE SUKAKSHI
Normal: ASAMASAME BUDDHAVILOKITE DHARMAPARIKSHITE
Normal: SANGHANIRGHOSHANI BHASHYA BHASHYA SHUHDI
Normal: MANTRA MANTRAAKSHAYATE RUTE RUTA KAUSHALYA
Normal: AKSHARA AKSHARA TYAYANTE ABHYAVAKARA AVALOKANI
Normal: "World-Honored One," Medicine King said, "this protection song, this powerful dhāraṇī, has been spoken by six hundred and twenty million Buddhas—as many Buddhas as there are grains of sand in the Ganges. Listen here: If anybody harms a teacher of this Dharma, they have harmed ALL THOSE BUDDHAS. You understand what I'm saying? You touch one of ours, you touch the whole family."
Heading 2: THE BUDDHA SAYS AMEN
Normal: Then Śākyamuni Buddha praised Medicine King, saying: "Good, good! Medicine King, you done right. Because you have compassion for these Dharma teachers, because you want to protect them, you spoke this dhāraṇī. And it's gonna bring great benefit to all living beings. Great benefit indeed."

Normal: And he spoke the powerful words:

Heading 2: WHEN THE GUARDIAN OF THE EAST JOINS IN

Normal: AGANE GANE GAURI GANDHARA CHANDALI

Heading 2: WHEN THE YAKSHA GODDESSES SWEAR THEIR OATH
Normal: Right then there were ten yaksha goddesses—now these are fierce female spirits, you understand—and their names were:

Normal: "World-Honored One, we too want to protect those who read and recite and hold on to the Lotus teaching. We want to remove their troubles. If anyone is looking for a way to harm a Dharma teacher, they won't find it. We won't let them find it."

Normal: Like the disaster of pressing out oil with false measures,
Normal: Like cheating people with crooked scales,
Normal: Like Devadatta breaking up the Sangha—
Normal: That's the kind of disaster you'll bring on yourself
Normal: If you harm a teacher of this Dharma.
Heading 2: THE YAKSHA GODDESSES MAKE THEIR PROMISE
Normal: When those yaksha goddesses had spoken this verse, they said to the Buddha:
Normal: "World-Honored One, we ourselves will personally protect those who hold and read and recite and practice this teaching. We'll give them peace and security. We'll keep all troubles away. We'll neutralize all poisons."
Normal: And the Buddha said to those yaksha goddesses: "Good, good! Listen now: If you all can protect even someone who just holds on to the NAME of the Lotus teaching—just the name!—your merit is beyond measure. How much more if you protect someone who fully holds on to this teaching, who makes offerings to these written scrolls with flowers, incense, necklaces, powdered incense, paste incense, burning incense, with banners and canopies, with music, with all kinds of lamps—butter lamps, oil lamps, fragrant oil lamps, jasmine oil lamps, champaka flower oil lamps, varshika flower oil lamps, utpala water lily oil lamps—with these hundred thousand kinds of offerings!
Normal: "Kuntī, you and all your attendants should protect such teachers of the Dharma. You hear what I'm saying? Protect them."
Heading 2: WHAT HAPPENED WHEN THEY HEARD THIS
Normal: When this Protection Songs chapter was spoken, sixty-eight thousand people—that's right, sixty-eight thousand souls—attained the patience of non-arising. That means they reached the place where they knew: Nothing is born, nothing dies, it all just keeps flowing. They got free right then, just from hearing about this protection.
Normal: END OF CHAPTER TWENTY-SIX: THE PROTECTION SONGS
Heading 2: INTERPRETATION NOTES:
Normal: This chapter reveals the other face of compassion: FIERCE PROTECTION. This is the love that says, "You will not harm my children." The dhāraṇī, or protection songs, are not translated because they are sounds of power, meant to be uttered, not intellectually understood. Their power is in the sound itself.
Normal: The key principle is cosmic justice: "If you harm a teacher of this Dharma, you have harmed all those Buddhas." It's a declaration that those who speak truth are BACKED UP by the entire cosmos. Even former demons like the yaksha goddesses and Hariti become protectors, showing that the Dharma is so universal it can transform even the wildest forces to serve the good.
Normal: The oaths and curses sworn by the yaksha goddesses are not petty threats but a form of sacred covenant, demonstrating the profound seriousness of protecting the Dharma. This chapter is permission to stand up and speak truth without fear, knowing that the universe itself stands guard.
Heading 1: CHAPTER TWENTY-SEVEN: THE BEAUTIFUL KING AND HIS GOOD FRIENDS
Normal: A Blues Interpretation from the Classical Chinese
Heading 2: A STORY ABOUT LOVE THAT WON'T LET YOU STAY LOST
Normal: Listen now, the Buddha stood before that great crowd and he told them straight:
Normal: "Way back, so far back you can't count it—more lifetimes ago than there are grains of sand in all the rivers that ever run—there was a Buddha named Cloud-Thunder-Sound-Ancient-King-Flower-Wisdom, the Tathāgata, the Arhat, the Perfectly Enlightened One. His land was called Light-Bright-Adorned, and that age, that time, they called it the Age of Joy-Seeing.
Normal: "Now in that Buddha's teaching, there was a king. They called him Beautiful King. And his queen, she went by the name Pure Virtue. They had two boys—one named Pure Storehouse, the other called Pure Eye. And listen here, these two boys, they weren't no ordinary children. No sir. They had great spiritual power. They had merit and wisdom built up deep. They'd been walking that Bodhisattva road for a long, long time, you understand? They knew all about giving and virtue and patience and effort and meditation and wisdom. They knew about skillful means. They understood compassion and joy and equanimity—all thirty-seven paths that help you along the way, they had those down cold. They could enter all kinds of deep meditation states—the Pure Samadhi, the Sun-Star-Dwelling Samadhi, the Pure Light Samadhi, the Pure Color Samadhi, the Pure Illuminating Samadhi, the Long-Adorning Samadhi, the Great-Mighty-Virtue-Treasury Samadhi. All these deep stillnesses, they knew them through and through.
Normal: "Now that Buddha, Cloud-Thunder-Sound-Ancient-King-Flower-Wisdom, he wanted to guide that Beautiful King onto the right path. He had compassion for all living beings, you see. So he preached this Lotus Sutra, this very teaching right here.
Normal: "And when he did, those two boys—Pure Storehouse and Pure Eye—they went to their mama. They put their palms together, fingers all joined up respectful-like, and they said: 'Mama, we wish you would go see that Buddha, Cloud-Thunder-Sound-Ancient-King-Flower-Wisdom. We want to go with you, serve him, honor him, bow down before him. You know why? Because this Buddha, he's teaching this Lotus Sutra right now to all the heavenly beings and all the human folks. We need to hear it. We got to receive it.'
Normal: "Their mama, she looked at them boys and said: 'Your daddy, he believes in outside teachings. He's deep into that Brahmin religion, got it in his bones. Y'all need to go talk to your father, see if he'll come along with us.'
Normal: "Pure Storehouse and Pure Eye, they put their hands together again and said to their mama: 'Mama, we are sons of the Dharma King. But we been born into this house of wrong views.'
Normal: "Their mother said: 'You boys need to think about your father. You need to show him some supernatural signs, some wonders. If he can see something that shakes him, his heart might get clear. His mind might get pure. Then maybe he'll let us go to where that Buddha is.'
Normal: "So those two sons, thinking about their daddy, they rose up into the air. They went up high—seven palm-tree heights into the sky. And then they started showing all kinds of miraculous transformations. Up there in space, they walked and they stood and they sat and they lay down. Water poured out the top of their bodies while fire blazed from their feet. Then water poured from their feet while fire blazed from their heads. One minute they got huge, filling up the whole sky. Next minute they got tiny as a mustard seed. Then huge again. Then small. They disappeared in the air and suddenly showed up on the ground. They walked into earth like it was water. They walked on water like it was solid ground. They showed all manner of supernatural wonders like this, trying to make their father's heart clean, trying to make his mind believe.
Normal: "When that father-king saw what his sons could do, his heart filled up with joy—great joy he'd never felt before. He put his palms together toward his boys and said: 'Who is your teacher? Whose disciples are you?'
Normal: "The two sons answered: 'Great King, that Buddha Cloud-Thunder-Sound-Ancient-King-Flower-Wisdom—right now he's sitting under the seven-jeweled enlightenment tree on the Dharma seat, and he's teaching this Lotus Sutra to all the gods and humans gathered there. He is our teacher. We are his students.'
Normal: "The father said to his sons: 'I want to see your teacher too. Let's all go together.'
Normal: "So those two boys came down from the sky and went to their mother. They put their palms together and said: 'Mama, Daddy's heart is open now. He's ready to awaken to supreme perfect enlightenment. We've done the Buddha's work for our father. Now please, Mama, let us leave home and practice the way under that Buddha.'
Normal: Mama, please let us go,
Normal: Let us leave this home, become monks on the road,
Normal: Buddhas are hard to find, Mama, harder than you know,
Normal: We gonna follow this Buddha wherever he goes.
Normal: Like that udumbara flower—you might wait forever,
Normal: Meeting a Buddha is rarer than rare, now or never,
Normal: Getting free from suffering, that's hard too,
Normal: Mama, please let us go, let us walk this path through.
Normal: "Their mother said right away: 'I'll let you leave home. You know why? Because Buddhas are hard to meet, that's why.'
Normal: "Then the two boys spoke to both their parents: 'Good! Good, Father! Good, Mother! Please, let's go right now to see Cloud-Thunder-Sound-Ancient-King-Flower-Wisdom Buddha. Let's get close to him, serve him, honor him. You know why we're saying this? Because a Buddha is hard to meet—rare as the udumbara flower that blooms once in forever. Rare as a one-eyed turtle swimming in the ocean who happens to stick his head up through the hole in a floating log. But we got deep blessings from past lives, and we been born in a time when Buddha-teaching is alive. So Father, Mother, you got to let us leave home. Why? Because Buddhas are hard to meet, and the time when they're here don't come around often.'
Normal: "Now at that time, Beautiful King had eighty-four thousand women in his palace, and every single one of them was ready to receive and hold this Lotus Sutra. Pure Eye Bodhisattva had long been deep in the Lotus Samadhi. Pure Storehouse Bodhisattva had, for countless hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of lifetimes, been deep in the Samadhi of Leaving All Evil Destinies—he wanted to help all beings escape suffering, you see. And the king's wife, Pure Virtue, she had the Samadhi Where All Buddhas Gather. She could know the secret treasuries of all the Buddhas.
Normal: "So those two sons used skillful means. They taught their father well. They made his heart believe. They made him love the Buddha's way.
Normal: "Then Beautiful King, along with all his ministers and attendants, and Pure Virtue the queen, along with all the palace women, and the king's two sons, along with forty-two thousand people—all of them together, at the same time, went to where the Buddha was. When they got there, they bowed their heads to his feet, walked around him three times to the right, then stood to one side.
Normal: "That Buddha preached the Dharma to the king. He showed him, taught him, benefited him, gladdened him. The king's heart filled up with joy.
Normal: "Then Beautiful King and his wife took off the pearl necklaces from around their necks—worth a hundred thousand in value—and scattered them over the Buddha. Up there in space, those necklaces turned into a four-pillared jeweled pavilion. Inside that pavilion was a great jeweled bed covered with hundreds of thousands of millions of heavenly cloths. On top of that bed sat a Buddha in full lotus position, shining great light.
Normal: "Beautiful King thought to himself: 'The Buddha's body—it's so rare, so dignified, so special. It's accomplished the most subtle and wonderful form there is.'
Normal: "Then Cloud-Thunder-Sound-Ancient-King-Flower-Wisdom Buddha said to the four assemblies: 'Y'all see this Beautiful King standing here before me with his palms together? This king is gonna practice as a monk in my teaching. He's gonna work hard, gonna help the Buddha way. And he's gonna become a Buddha called Sal-Tree King. His land will be called Great Light, and that age will be called Great High King. That Sal-Tree King Buddha will have countless Bodhisattvas and countless disciples. His land will be level and straight. His merit will be like this.'
Normal: "Right then and there, the king handed his kingdom over to his younger brother. Then he and his wife and his two sons and all his relatives left home in the Buddha's teaching to practice the way.
Normal: "After the king left home, for eighty-four thousand years he kept at it, steady and hard, practicing this Wonderful Lotus Sutra. After that time passed, he gained the Samadhi of All Pure Merit Adornment. He rose up into space, seven palm-tree heights high, and said to the Buddha: 'World-Honored One, these two sons of mine have done the Buddha's work. Through supernatural transformations, they turned my wrong-headed mind around. They helped me settle down safe in the Buddha's teaching. They helped me see the World-Honored One. These two sons are my good spiritual friends. They wanted to wake up the good roots I'd planted in past lives. They wanted to benefit me. So they came and were born into my house.'
Normal: "Then Cloud-Thunder-Sound-Ancient-King-Flower-Wisdom Buddha said to Beautiful King: 'That's right. That's exactly right. Just like you said. When good men and good women plant good roots, life after life they meet good spiritual friends. And those good spiritual friends do the Buddha's work—they show, they teach, they benefit, they gladden, they help folks enter supreme perfect enlightenment. Great King, you need to know: good spiritual friends are the great cause, the great condition. They guide you, they help you see a Buddha, they help you awaken the mind of supreme perfect enlightenment.
Normal: "'Great King, you see these two sons of yours? These two sons have already served and honored sixty-five hundred thousand million billion nayuta Ganges-sands of Buddhas. They've been close to all those Buddhas, respectful to all those Buddhas. In all those Buddha-places, they've received and held this Lotus Sutra. They have compassion for beings trapped in wrong views. They want to help people dwell in right seeing.'
Normal: "Beautiful King came down from space and said to the Buddha: 'World-Honored One, the Tathāgata is so rare. Because of your merit and wisdom, the flesh-bump on top of your head shines bright. Your eyes are long and wide and deep blue. The mark between your eyebrows is white like the bright moon. Your teeth are white and even and always shining. Your lips are red and beautiful like the bimba fruit.'
Normal: "Then Beautiful King praised the Buddha's countless hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of virtues like this. Standing before the Tathāgata, with his palms joined together as one, he said again: 'World-Honored One, this has never happened before. The Tathāgata's teaching is complete, accomplished with inconceivable subtle and wonderful merit. The precepts and training you give—they're safe, they're peaceful, they're good. From this day forward, I will not follow my own mind's desires. I will not give birth to wrong views, arrogance, anger, or any evil thoughts.'
Normal: "When he finished saying this, he bowed to the Buddha and left.
Normal: The Buddha told the great assembly:
Normal: "What do y'all think? Was Beautiful King some other person? No. He is now Flower Virtue Bodhisattva right here. And Pure Virtue, his wife—she is now the Bodhisattva Light-Shining-Adornment-Mark who's here before this Buddha. Out of compassion for Beautiful King and all his relatives, she was born into that world then.
Normal: "And those two sons? They are now Medicine King Bodhisattva and Medicine Superior Bodhisattva. These two Bodhisattvas—Medicine King and Medicine Superior—have accomplished great merit like this. They have planted roots of virtue under countless hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of Buddhas. They have accomplished inconceivable good merits.
Normal: "If anyone knows the names of these two Bodhisattvas, all the gods and humans in all the worlds should bow down to them in respect."
Normal: When the Buddha finished speaking this chapter about the past deeds of Beautiful King, eighty-four thousand people brushed off the dust, left the dirt behind, and gained the pure Dharma eye in all teachings.
Normal: END OF CHAPTER TWENTY-SEVEN: THE BEAUTIFUL KING AND HIS GOOD FRIENDS
Heading 2: INTERPRETATION NOTES:
Normal: This chapter's teaching that "good spiritual friends are the great cause" is pure blues theology. We don't wake up alone. We wake up because somebody loved us enough to not let us sleep through our lives. The teaching comes from the most intimate place possible—from family. The two sons, who are revealed to be Medicine King and Medicine Superior, are willing to be born into a household of "wrong views" to save their father.
Normal: The supernatural displays are not about intimidation; they are about breaking the king's frame of what he thinks is possible, to make him receptive to the Dharma. The story teaches that love is persistent, and that grace can show up in the form of your own children, your spouse, or your friends, working patiently to guide you home.
Normal: The final revelation—that these figures from the past are bodhisattvas present in the assembly now—reinforces the Lotus Sutra's theme that the help you need is already here, and that compassion operates across countless lifetimes.
Heading 1: CHAPTER TWENTY-EIGHT: UNIVERSAL WORTHY COMES TO ENCOURAGE YOU
Normal: A Blues Interpretation from the Classical Chinese
Heading 2: THE FINAL WORD: YOU ARE NOT ALONE, YOU WILL AWAKEN
Normal: Listen now to how it all ends, how the whole teaching comes to its close:
Normal: At that time, Universal Worthy Bodhisattva—riding on his own sovereign supernatural power, carried by his mighty virtue and his name that's known throughout all worlds—he came from the East with countless, boundless, can't-be-numbered great Bodhisattvas. And listen, everywhere those beings passed through on their journey, all those countries shook and trembled. Jeweled lotus flowers rained down from the sky. A hundred thousand million billion kinds of music played—not human music, understand, but cosmic music, the sound the universe makes when grace is moving.
Normal: And he didn't come alone. No sir. He brought with him numberless gods, dragons, night-wanderers, gandharvas, asuras, garudas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans and non-humans—all of them surrounding him, every one of them showing their own power and virtue and supernatural might. They all came to this Saha world, to Vulture Peak Mountain. When they got there, they bowed their heads to the ground before Śākyamuni Buddha. They walked around him seven times to the right, and then Universal Worthy said to the Buddha:
Normal: "World-Honored One, I was in the land of Precious Majesty Superior King Buddha, and way over there I heard that in this Saha world you were preaching this Lotus Sutra. So I came with these countless, boundless, hundred thousand million billion Bodhisattvas to listen and receive it. I'm asking you, World-Honored One—please tell us: After the Tathāgata passes away, when you're gone from this world, how can good men and good women get hold of this Lotus Sutra? How do they receive it?"
Normal: The Buddha told Universal Worthy Bodhisattva:
Normal: "If good men and good women accomplish four things, then after the Tathāgata passes away, they WILL get this Lotus Sutra. Listen to what these four things are:
Normal: "First: They're protected and kept in mind by all the Buddhas.
Normal: "Second: They've planted roots of virtue, built up good deep in themselves.
Normal: "Third: They've entered the company of those who are fixed on the right path, who are determined, who won't turn back.
Normal: "Fourth: They've aroused the mind that wants to save ALL living beings—every last one.
Normal: "Good men and good women who accomplish these four things—after the Tathāgata passes away, they WILL get this sutra. Count on it. It's guaranteed."
Normal: Then Universal Worthy Bodhisattva said to the Buddha:
Normal: "World-Honored One, in the last five hundred years, in that polluted evil age that's coming, whoever receives and holds this sutra—I WILL guard them. I will protect them. I will remove their troubles and their dangers. I will give them peace and safety. I will make sure that nothing—NOTHING—can find a way to harm them.
Normal: "No demons, no demons' sons, no demons' daughters, no demon-followers, no demon-possessed people. No night-wanderers, no rakshasas, no kumbhandas, no pishachas, no krityas, no putanas, no vetadas—none of these beings that trouble people will be able to take advantage of them.
Normal: "Whether that person is walking or standing still, whether they're reading this sutra or reciting it—at that time I will ride my six-tusked white elephant king. I will come with a great company of Bodhisattvas to where that person is. I will show myself to them. I will make offerings to them. I will guard them. I will comfort their hearts. You know why I'll do all this? Because I'm also making offerings to the Lotus Sutra itself.
Normal: "And if that person is sitting down, thinking about this sutra, meditating on it—at that time I will ride that white elephant king again and appear before them. If they forget even one sentence, one verse of the Lotus Sutra, I WILL teach it to them. I will recite it together with them. I will help them understand it thoroughly.
Normal: "And when that person who receives and holds and reads and recites the Lotus Sutra sees me, they will be filled with great joy—the kind of joy that makes you want to keep going. And because they see me, right then and there they will gain samādhis and dhāraṇīs. They'll gain the Revolving Dharani, the Hundred Thousand Million Billion Revolving Dharani, the Dharani of Skillful Means in the Sound of the Teaching. They'll get dhāraṇīs like these."
Normal: "World-Honored One, in that later age, in the last five hundred years, in that polluted evil world—if there are monks, nuns, laymen, or laywomen who seek this teaching, who receive it, who read it, who recite it, who copy it down, if they want to practice this Lotus Sutra—they should focus themselves single-mindedly for three weeks. Twenty-one days.
Normal: "When those three weeks are completed, I will ride my six-tusked white elephant. I will come with countless Bodhisattvas surrounding me. I will appear to that person in a body that all beings love to see. I will preach the Dharma to them. I will show them. I will teach them. I will benefit them. I will make them glad. And I will also give them dhāraṇī-mantras.
Normal: "And when they get these dhāraṇīs, no non-human being will be able to break them. No woman will be able to lead them astray. I myself will always guard that person.
Normal: "So World-Honored One, please let me speak this dhāraṇī-mantra."
Normal: Then right there, standing before the Buddha, he spoke the mantra:
Normal: Atandi / Tandavabha-di / Tandavabha-te / Tanda-kusalai / Tanda-sudalai / Sudalai / Sudara-vabha-te-buddha-pashane / Sarva-dhāraṇī-avabha-tani / Sarva-bhasha-avabha-tani / Shu-avabha-tani / Sengha-pariksha-ni / Sengha-nirgha-tani / Asengi / Sengha-bhaga-di / Taile-ayuta-sengha-dutale / Arati-barati / Sarva-sengha-samadi-galan-di / Sarva-dharma-shubha-lishate / Sarva-sattva-rutaka-ushalya-anumga-di / Shen-avi-kilidi-te
Normal: "World-Honored One, if any Bodhisattva hears this dhāraṇī, they should know it's the supernatural power of Universal Worthy at work. If this Lotus Sutra circulates in this Jambudvipa world, if anyone receives and holds it, they should think: 'This is ALL because of Universal Worthy's mighty spiritual power.'
Normal: "If anyone receives it, reads it, recites it, keeps it correctly in mind, understands its meaning, practices according to what it says—know that such a person is doing Universal Worthy's practice. They've planted deep roots of goodness before countless, boundless Buddhas. The Tathāgatas themselves have put their hands on that person's head.
Normal: "If someone just copies this sutra down, writes it out—when that person dies, they will be born in the Trayastrimsha Heaven. At that time, eighty-four thousand heavenly women will come to greet them, playing all kinds of music. That person will wear a crown made of seven jewels, and there among those palace women they will experience joy and happiness. How much more so for those who receive it, hold it, read it, recite it, keep it correctly in mind, and practice according to what it says!
Normal: "If anyone receives and holds this teaching, reads and recites it, understands its meaning—when that person's life ends, a thousand Buddhas will reach out their hands to them. They won't be afraid. They won't fall into evil destinies. They will go straight to Tushita Heaven, to where Maitreya Bodhisattva is. Maitreya Bodhisattva has the thirty-two marks of a great being. He's surrounded by a great assembly of Bodhisattvas. He's attended by hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of heavenly women. That person will be born right there in that company. These are the kinds of merits and benefits they'll receive.
Normal: "So if you're wise, you should single-mindedly copy this sutra yourself, or have someone else copy it. You should receive it, hold it, read it, recite it, keep it correctly in mind, and practice according to what it says.
Normal: "World-Honored One, I will now use my supernatural powers to guard this sutra. After the Tathāgata passes away, I will cause it to spread widely throughout this Jambudvipa. I will make sure it never dies out."
Normal: At that time Śākyamuni Buddha praised him, saying:
Normal: "Excellent! Excellent, Universal Worthy! You can protect and help this sutra, causing many beings to gain peace, benefit, and happiness. You have already accomplished inconceivable merit and deep great compassion. From the distant past you have aroused the mind of supreme perfect enlightenment, and now you are able to make this supernatural vow to guard this sutra.
Normal: "I will use my own supernatural power to guard and protect anyone who can receive and hold the name of Bodhisattva Universal Worthy."
Normal: "Universal Worthy, if anyone receives, holds, reads, recites, keeps correctly in mind, practices, and copies this Lotus Sutra—know that such a person SEES Śākyamuni Buddha. It's as if they hear this sutra directly from the Buddha's mouth.
Normal: "Know that such a person is MAKING OFFERINGS to Śākyamuni Buddha.
Normal: "Know that the Buddha is saying to them: 'Excellent! Well done!'
Normal: "Know that Śākyamuni Buddha is placing his hand on that person's head.
Normal: "Know that Śākyamuni Buddha's robe is covering them, protecting them.
Normal: "Such a person will no longer be greedy for worldly pleasures. They won't like the scriptures or writings of non-Buddhist paths. They won't take pleasure in getting close to such people or to those who do evil—butchers, those who raise pigs, sheep, chickens, or dogs, hunters, those who sell sex.
Normal: "That person's mind and intentions will be straight and true. They will have right mindfulness. They will have the power of merit and virtue.
Normal: "That person will not be troubled by the three poisons. They also will not be troubled by jealousy, arrogance, self-deception, or inflated pride.
Normal: "That person will have few desires. They will know contentment. They will be able to practice Universal Worthy's way."
Normal: "Universal Worthy, after the Tathāgata passes away, in the last five hundred years—if anyone sees someone who receives, holds, reads, and recites the Lotus Sutra, they should think:
Normal: 'This person will not be long in going to the place of enlightenment. This person is about to break through all the demon armies. This person is about to attain supreme perfect enlightenment. This person is about to turn the Dharma wheel, beat the Dharma drum, blow the Dharma conch, rain down the Dharma rain. This person is about to sit on the lion throne of Dharma in the great assembly of gods and humans.'
Normal: "Universal Worthy, if in later ages anyone receives, holds, reads, and recites this sutra—that person will no longer be greedy for clothes, bedding, food, drink, or the things that sustain life. Their wishes will not be empty. Even in this present life they will receive the rewards of blessing.
Normal: "If anyone slights and insults them, saying 'You're just a crazy person! You do this practice for nothing! In the end you'll gain nothing!'—the karmic retribution for speaking like that is this: that person will be eyeless, blind, world after world after world.
Normal: "But if anyone makes offerings to them and praises them, they will see the fruit of that reward in this very life.
Normal: "If anyone sees someone who receives and holds this sutra and exposes their faults—whether those faults are real or made up—that person in this present life will get white leprosy.
Normal: "If anyone mocks and laughs at them, that person world after world will have gapped and broken teeth, ugly lips, a flat nose, twisted hands and feet, squinting eyes, a body that stinks, evil sores, pus and blood, bloated belly, short breath, and all kinds of severe and evil diseases.
Normal: "Therefore, Universal Worthy, if you see anyone who receives and holds this sutra, you should rise up and go meet them from far away. You should respect them just as you would respect a Buddha."
Normal: When the Buddha spoke this Chapter of Universal Worthy's Encouragement, Bodhisattvas countless as the sands of the Ganges River gained hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of Revolving Dharanis. Bodhisattvas as numerous as the dust motes in a great thousand-fold world system fully accomplished Universal Worthy's Way.
Normal: When the Buddha was speaking this sutra, Universal Worthy and all the other Bodhisattvas, Śāriputra and all the other disciples, and the gods, dragons, humans, non-humans, and everyone in that entire great assembly—they all received it with great joy. They accepted and held the Buddha's words. They bowed in respect and departed.
Normal: END OF CHAPTER TWENTY-EIGHT: UNIVERSAL WORTHY COMES TO ENCOURAGE YOU
Heading 2: INTERPRETATION NOTES:
Normal: This final chapter is the ultimate encouragement. After all the teachings, parables, and cosmic displays, Universal Worthy Bodhisattva arrives from the East to make a personal promise: he will protect anyone who holds this sutra in the difficult ages to come. He is the guarantor, the protector, the one who ensures the teaching will not be lost.
Normal: The four conditions for receiving the sutra are a summary of the path: 1) Be mindful of the Buddhas, 2) Plant good roots, 3) Enter the correct concentration, and 4) Arouse the mind to save all beings. This isn't a passive reception; it's an active state of being.
Normal: Universal Worthy's vow to appear on his six-tusked white elephant to any practitioner who is struggling, who forgets a line, or who needs encouragement is one of the most intimate and comforting promises in the sutra. It says: you are not alone in your practice. When you sincerely engage with this teaching, help will come.
Normal: The chapter ends with a stark warning about the karmic consequences of slandering those who uphold the sutra (blindness, leprosy, etc.) and the immediate rewards for honoring them. This final section underscores the sutra's ultimate point: the teaching is not an abstract text, but a living reality embodied in the people who hold it. To honor them is to honor the Buddha himself.
